Subpart B - RELATED LAWS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note— Printed in this subpart B are local constitutional amendments applicable to the City of Lyons. The source of each amendment is stated in a history note following the provision. Obvious misspellings have been corrected without notation. For stylistic purposes, a uniform system of headings, catchlines and citations to state statutes has been used. Additions for clarity are indicated by brackets. 

Sec. 1. - Lyons Development Authority. 
A.  There is hereby created a body corporate and politic in the City of Lyons in Toombs County to be known as the Lyons Development Authority, which shall be an instrumentality of the City of Lyons and a public corporation and which in this amendment is hereafter referred to as the "Authority"; 
B.  The authority shall consist of five members who shall serve for a term of five years and who shall be eligible for reappointment. The members shall be appointed by the Mayor and Council of the City of Lyons. The first members shall be appointed for terms of one, two, three, four and five years, and thereafter their successors shall be appointed for terms of five years. Vacancies shall be filled for the unexpired term by the mayor and council. A majority of the members shall constitute a quorum and a majority may act for the authority in any matter. No vacancy shall impair the power of the authority to act. No member shall be mayor nor a member of the council of the City of Lyons, but there shall be no other disqualification to hold public office by reason of membership in the authority; 
C.  The property, obligations and the interest on the obligations of the authority shall have the same immunity from taxation as the property, obligations and interest on the obligations of the City of Lyons; 
The exemption from taxation herein provided shall not extend to tenants nor lessees of the authority. The right of any private person to use or occupy any real estate of the authority for a period of one year or longer under any lease or other agreement for the purposes of taxation shall be classed as an interest in the real estate and as real property and shall be taxed as real property as now provided by law, or may be taxed as the General Assembly may hereafter provide by general or local law. The tax exemption herein provided also shall not include exemption from sale and use taxes on property purchased by the authority or for use of the authority. 
D.  The powers of the authority shall include but not be limited to, the power: 
(1)  To buy, acquire, develop, improve, own[,] operate, maintain, sell[,] lease as lessor and lessee, and mortgage land, buildings and property of all kinds within the City of Lyons and also without the City of Lyons, but not beyond the limits of Toombs County; 
(2)  To receive and administer gifts, grants and donations and to administer trusts; 
(3)  To grant, loan and lease without adequate consideration or without any consideration and with and without security, any of its funds and property to private persons and corporations operating or proposing to operate any industrial plant or establishment within the City of Lyons or at any place within Toombs County sufficiently close to the City of Lyons to be of benefit to the people of the city in the judgment of the authority. The provisions of this clause shall not be construed to limit any other power of the authority; 
(4)  To borrow money and to issue notes, bonds and revenue certificates therefor and to sell, convey, mortgage, pledge and assign any and all of its funds, property and income as security therefor; 
(5)  To contract with the City of Lyons, other municipalities and other political subdivisions and with private persons and corporations and to sue and be sued in its corporate name; 
(6)  To have and exercise usual powers of private corporations except such as are inconsistent with this amendment, including the power to appoint and hire officers, agents and employees and to provide their compensation and duties, which officers and agents may or may not be members of the authority, and the power to adopt and amend a corporate seal and bylaws and regulations for the conduct and management of the authority; 
(7)  To encourage and promote the expansion of industry, agriculture, trade, commerce and recreation in the City of Lyons and in Toombs County, and to make long-range plans therefor; 
(8)  To exercise such other powers and duties as may be delegated to it by the Mayor and Council of the City of Lyons; 
(9)  To accumulate its funds from year to year and to invest accumulated funds in any manner that public funds of the State of Georgia or any of its political subdivisions may be invested; 
(10)  To designate officers to sign and act for the authority generally or in any specific matter; 
(11)  To do any and all acts and things necessary or convenient to accomplish the purpose and powers of the authority as herein stated. 
E.  The authority shall not be authorized to create in any manner any debt, liability or obligation, against the City of Lyons, the State of Georgia, nor Toombs County; 
F.  The authority shall have the same immunity and exemption from liability for torts and negligence as the State of Georgia and the officers, agents and employees of the authority when in performance of the work of the authority, shall have the same immunity and exemption from liability for torts and negligence as the officers, agents and employees of the State of Georgia when in performance of their public duties or work of the State. The authority may be sued the same as private corporations on any contractual obligation of the authority; 
G.  The members of the authority shall receive only such compensation for their services to the authority as shall be authorized by the Mayor and Council of the City of Lyons but such compensation shall be paid from the funds of the authority; 
H.  The City of Lyons is authorized to levy an annual tax, not to exceed one mill, in addition to all other taxes of whatever kind, on all taxable property within the city for the support of the authority and for its use and purposes, and all funds raised by such tax shall be paid and appropriated by the City of Lyons to the authority and when paid to the authority, shall become a part of its funds and may be used by it for any of its purposes and powers as herein provided or as may be hereafter provided by law, which tax shall be in addition to all other taxes authorized by law; 
I.  The City of Lyons is also authorized in addition to the tax provided in Paragraph H, to appropriate to the authority such amount from its funds each year as its governing authority and [sic] shall see fit but not exceeding ten percent of its total receipts from business licenses for the year, and any funds so appropriated when paid to the authority shall become a part of its funds and may be used by the authority in accordance with its powers and purposes as herein stated or as may be hereafter defined by law; 
J.  The property of the authority shall not be subject to levy and sale under legal process except such property, income or funds as may be pledged, assigned, mortgaged or conveyed to secure an obligation of the authority, and any such property, funds or income may be sold under the legal process or under any power granted by the authority to enforce payment of the obligation; 
K.  This amendment is adopted for the purpose of promoting and expanding for the public good and welfare of the City of Lyons and its citizens, industry, agriculture, trade, commerce and recreation within the City of Lyons and in Toombs County, and making of long-range plans for such development and expansion and to authorize the use of public funds of the City of Lyons for such purposes, and this amendment and any law enacted with reference to the authority shall be liberally construed for the accomplishment of this purpose; 
L.  This amendment shall be effective immediately upon proclamation of its ratification by the Governor and the first members of the authority shall be appointed within thirty days after such proclamation; 
M.  The General Assembly may by law further define and prescribe the powers and duties of the authority and the exercise thereof, and may enlarge and restrict the same, and may likewise further regulate the management and conduct of the authority. The authority shall be an instrumentality of the City of Lyons with power to extend its operations outside of the City of Lyons but not beyond the limits of Toombs County as herein provided, and the scope of its operations shall be limited to the territory embraced within Toombs County and the City of Lyons. The General Assembly shall not extend the jurisdiction of the authority nor the scope of its operations beyond the limits of the City of Lyons and Toombs County; 
N.  There shall be no limitation upon the amount of debt which the authority may incur, but no debt created by the authority shall be a debt of the City of Lyons, the State of Georgia, nor Toombs County. 
(1957 Ga. Laws (Act No. 29), page 181, § 1) 
Editor's note— The above amendment to Ga. Const. (1945) art. VII, § V, ¶ I, was continued by 1985 Ga. Laws (Act No. 327), page 4501. 
State Law reference— Development Authorities Law, O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq. 
RELATED LAWS COMPARATIVE TABLE GEORGIA LAWS 
This table gives the location of Georgia Laws in the Related Laws. 

 
Chapter 1 - GENERAL PROVISIONS 

Sec. 1-1. - Designation of and citation to Code. 
The ordinances embraced in this and the following chapters shall constitute and be designated "The Code of Lyons, Georgia," or "Lyons City Code" and may be so cited. 
(Code 1977, § 1-1) 
State Law reference— Ordinance codification, O.C.G.A. § 36-80-19. 
Sec. 1-2. - Definitions and rules of construction. 
In the construction of this Code and of all ordinances, the rules of construction and definitions set out in this section shall be observed. The rules of construction and definitions set out in this section shall not be applied to any section of this Code which shall contain any express provision excluding such construction or where the subject matter or context of such section may be repugnant thereto. 
Generally. The ordinary signification shall be applied to all words, except words of art or words connected with a particular trade or subject matter when they shall have the signification attached to them by experts in such trade or with reference to such subject matter. In all interpretations the courts shall look diligently for the intention of the city council, keeping in view, at all times, the old law, the evil and the remedy. Grammatical errors shall not vitiate, and a transposition of words and clauses may be resorted to when the sentence or clause is without meaning as it stands. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-1(a), (b). 
Liberal construction; minimum requirements; overlapping provisions. All general provisions, terms, phrases and expressions contained in this Code shall be liberally construed in order that the true intent and meaning of the city council may be fully carried out. In the interpretation and application of any section of this Code, they shall be held to be the minimum requirements adopted for the promotion of the public health, safety, comfort, convenience and general welfare. Where any section of this Code imposes greater restrictions upon the subject matter than the other sections of this Code, the section imposing the greater restriction or regulation shall be deemed to be controlling. The specific controls over the general. 
As soon as possible. The term "as soon as possible" means within a reasonable time, having due regard to all the circumstances. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3(5). 
Charter. The term "Charter" means the Charter of the City of Lyons, Georgia, as amended. 
City. The term "city" means the City of Lyons, Georgia. 
Code. The term "Code" means the Code of Lyons, Georgia, as designated in section 1-1. 
Computation of time. When a number of days is prescribed for the exercise of any privilege or the discharge of any duty, only the first or last day shall be counted. If the last day shall fall on Saturday or Sunday, the party having such privilege or duty shall have through the following Monday to exercise such privilege or to discharge the duty. When the last day prescribed for such action shall fall on a public or legal holiday as set forth in state law, the party having such privilege or duty shall have through the following business day to exercise such privilege or to discharge the duty. When the period of time prescribed is less than seven days, an intermediate Saturday, Sunday and legal holiday shall be excluded in the computation. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-1(3). 
Conjunctions. Where a provision involves two or more items, conditions, provisions or events connected by the conjunction "and," "or" or "either … or," the conjunction shall be interpreted as follows: 
(1)  The term "and" indicates that all the connected items, conditions, provisions or events shall apply. 
(2)  The term "or" indicates that the connected items, conditions, provisions or events may apply singly or in any combination. 
(3)  The term "either … or indicates that the connected items, conditions, provisions or events shall apply singly, but not in combination. 
Council, city council. The terms "council" and "city council" mean the city council of the City of Lyons, Georgia. 
County. The term "county" means Toombs County, Georgia. 
Delegation of authority. Whenever a section appears requiring a city officer or city employee to do some act, it is to be construed to authorize the officer or employee to designate, delegate and authorize subordinates to perform the required act. 
Following. The term "following" means next after. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3(8). 
Gender. Words of one gender include all other genders. 
State Law reference— Gender, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-1(4). 
Joint authority. A joint authority given to any number of persons or officers may be executed by a majority of them, unless it is otherwise declared. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-1(5). 
Keeper and proprietor. The terms "keeper" and "proprietor" mean and include persons, whether acting by themselves or acting as a servant, agent or employee. 
May. The term "may" is to be construed as being permissive. 
State Law reference— Definition of "may," O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3(10). 
Month. The term "month" means a calendar month. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3(11). 
Must. The term "must" is to be construed as being mandatory. 
Number. The singular and plural number include the other, unless expressly excluded. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-1(6). 
Oath. The term "oath" includes an affirmation. A solemn affirmation is the equivalent to an oath, and a person shall be deemed to have sworn if such person makes such an affirmation. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3(12). 
O.C.G.A. The abbreviation "O.C.G.A." means the Official Code of Georgia Annotated, as amended. 
Officials, employees, boards, commissions or other agencies. A reference to an official, employee, board, commission or other agency by title only, refers to the official, employee, board, commission or other agency of the city. 
Owner. The term "owner," as applied to a building or land, includes any part owner, joint owner, tenant in common, tenant in partnership or joint tenant of the whole or of a part of the building or land. 
Person. The term "person" includes any association, club, society, firm, corporation, partnership, body politic and corporate, as well as an individual. 
State Law reference— Definition of "person," O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3(14). 
Personal property. The term "personal property" includes every species of property, except real property. 
Preceding. The term "preceding" means next before. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3(15). 
Property. The term "property" includes real and personal property. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3(16). 
Public place. The term "public place" includes any place that the public is invited or permitted to go or congregate. 
Real property. The term "real property" include lands, tenements and hereditaments. 
Shall. The term "shall" is to be construed as being mandatory. 
Sidewalk. The term "sidewalk" means any portion of a street between the curbline and the adjacent property line, intended for the use of pedestrians, excluding parkways. 
Signature, subscription. The terms "signature" and "subscription" include the mark of an illiterate or infirm person. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3(19). 
State. The term "state" means the State of Georgia. 
Street or road. The term "street" or "road" includes any street, avenue, boulevard, road, alley, lane, viaduct and any other public highway in the city, including but not limited to, the paved or improved surfaces thereof. 
Tenant, occupant. The terms "tenant" and "occupant," applied to a building or land, include any person holding a written or oral lease or who occupies the whole or a part of a building or land, either alone or with others. 
Tense. Words used in the past or present tense include the future, as well as the past and present. 
State Law reference— Tense of words, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-1(7). 
Week. The term "week" means seven days. 
Will. The term "will" is to be construed as being mandatory. 
Writing. The term "writing" includes printing and all numerals. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3(23). 
Year. The term "year" means a calendar year. 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3(24). 
(Code 1977, § 1-2) 
Sec. 1-3. - Catchlines of sections; effect of history notes; references in Code. 
(a)  The catchlines of the several sections of this Code in boldface type are intended as mere catchwords to indicate the contents of the sections and shall not be deemed or taken to be titles of such sections nor as any part of such sections nor, unless expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when any of such sections, including the catchline, is amended or reenacted. 
(b)  The history or source notes appearing in parentheses after sections in this Code are not intended to have any legal effect but are merely intended to indicate the source of matter contained in the section. Cross references, Charter references, related law references and state law references which appear after sections or subsections of this Code or which otherwise appear in footnote form are provided for the convenience of the user of this Code and have no legal effect. 
(c)  All references to chapters, articles, divisions, subdivisions or sections are to chapters, articles, divisions, subdivisions or sections of this Code, unless otherwise specified. 
(Code 1977, § 1-3) 
Sec. 1-4. - Effect of repeal of ordinances. 
(a)  Unless specifically provided otherwise, the repeal of an ordinance does not revive any repealed ordinance. 
(b)  The repeal or amendment of an ordinance does not affect any punishment or penalty incurred before the repeal took effect, nor does such repeal or amendment affect any suit, prosecution or proceeding pending at the time of the amendment or repeal. 
(Code 1977, § 1-4) 
Sec. 1-5. - Amendments to Code; effect of new ordinances; amendatory language. 
(a)  All ordinances passed subsequent to this Code which amend, repeal or in any way affect this Code may be numbered in accordance with the numbering system of this Code and printed for inclusion in this Code. Repealed chapters, sections and subsections or any part thereof, by subsequent ordinances, may be excluded from the Code by omission from reprinted pages affected thereby. The subsequent ordinances as numbered and printed or omitted, in the case of repeal, shall be prima facie evidence of these subsequent ordinances until such time that this Code and subsequent ordinances numbered or omitted are readopted as a new code. 
(b)  Amendments to any of the sections of this Code may be made by amending those sections by specific reference to the section number of this Code in the following language: 
"Section _____ of The Code of Lyons, Georgia, is hereby amended to read as follows:…." The new provisions may then be set out in full as desired. 
(c)  If a new section not heretofore existing in the Code is to be added, the following language may be used: 
"The Code of Lyons, Georgia, is hereby amended by adding a section (or article or chapter) to be numbered _____, which section reads as follows:…." The new section may then be set out in full as desired. 
(d)  All sections, articles, chapters or provisions desired to be repealed should be specifically repealed by section, article or chapter number, as the case may be, or by setting them out at length in the repealing ordinance. 
(Code 1977, § 1-6) 
Sec. 1-6. - Supplementation of Code. 
(a)  Supplements to this Code shall be prepared and printed whenever authorized or directed by the city. A supplement to the Code shall include all substantive permanent and general parts of ordinances adopted during the period covered by the supplement and all changes made thereby in the Code. The pages of a supplement shall be so numbered that they will fit properly into the Code and will, where necessary, replace pages which have become obsolete or partially obsolete, and the new pages shall be so prepared that, when they have been inserted, the Code will be current through the date of the adoption of the latest ordinance included in the supplement. 
(b)  In preparing a supplement to this Code, all portions of the Code which have been repealed shall be excluded from the Code by the omission thereof from reprinted pages. 
(c)  When preparing a supplement to this Code, the person authorized to prepare the supplement may make formal, nonsubstantive changes in ordinances and parts of ordinances included in the supplement, insofar as it is necessary to do so to embody them into a unified Code. For example, the person may: 
(1)  Organize the ordinance material into appropriate subdivisions; 
(2)  Provide appropriate catchlines, headings and titles for sections and other subdivisions of the Code printed in the supplement and make changes in such catchlines, headings and titles; 
(3)  Assign appropriate numbers to sections and other subdivisions to be inserted in the Code and, where necessary to accommodate new material, change existing section or other subdivision numbers; 
(4)  Change the words "this ordinance" or words of the same meaning to "this chapter," "this article," "this division," etc., as the case may be, or to "sections _____ to _____" (inserting section numbers to indicate the sections of the Code which embody the substantive sections of the ordinance incorporated into the Code); and 
(5)  Make other nonsubstantive changes necessary to preserve the original meaning of ordinance sections inserted into the Code; but in no case shall the person make any change in the meaning or effect of ordinance material included in the supplement or already embodied in the Code. 
Sec. 1-7. - General penalty; continuing violations. 
(a)  In this section, the term "violation of this Code" means: 
(1)  Doing an act that is prohibited or made or declared unlawful, an offense or a misdemeanor by ordinance or by rule or regulation authorized by ordinance; 
(2)  Failure to perform an act that is required to be performed by ordinance or by rule or regulation authorized by ordinance; or 
(3)  Failure to perform an act if the failure is declared a misdemeanor or an offense or unlawful by ordinance or by rule or regulation authorized by ordinance. 
(b)  In this section, the term "violation of this Code" does not include the failure of a city officer or city employee to perform an official duty, unless it is provided that failure to perform the duty is to be punished as provided in this section or it is clear from the context that it is the intent to impose the penalty provided for in this section upon the officer or employee. 
(c)  Except as otherwise provided, a person convicted of a violation of this Code shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $300.00 or imprisonment for a term not exceeding 60 days or to work on the streets for a period not exceeding 60 days or any combination thereof. With respect to violations of this Code that are continuous with respect to time, each day the violation continues is a separate offense. With respect to violations of this Code that are not continuous with respect to time, each act constitutes a separate offense. 
(d)  The imposition of a penalty does not prevent revocation or suspension of a license, permit or franchise or other administrative sanctions. 
(e)  Violations of this Code that are continuous with respect to time are a public nuisance and may be abated by injunctive or other equitable relief and by such other means as are provided by law. The imposition of a penalty does not prevent equitable relief. 
(Code 1977, § 1-8) 
Charter reference— Maximum penalties authorized in municipal court, § 15. 
State Law reference— Limitations on penalties, O.C.G.A. § 36-35-6(a)(2). 
Sec. 1-8. - Appearance or bail bonds. 
The amounts of appearance or bail bonds for offenses against the city shall be as prescribed by the municipal judge. 
(Code 1977, § 1-9) 
Charter reference— Bonds to be approved by municipal judge, § 16. 
Sec. 1-9. - Severability of Code. 
The sections, paragraphs, sentences, clauses and phrases of this Code are severable, and if any phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph or section of this Code shall be declared unconstitutional, invalid or otherwise unenforceable by the valid judgment or decree of any court of competent jurisdiction, that unconstitutionality, invalidity or unenforceability shall not affect any of the remaining phrases, clauses, sentences, paragraphs or sections of this Code, since they would have been enacted without the incorporation in this Code of the unconstitutional, invalid or unenforceable phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph or section. 
(Code 1977, § 1-5) 
Sec. 1-10. - Continuation of existing ordinances. 
The sections appearing in this Code, insofar as they are the same as those of the Code of the city, as amended, and ordinances existing at the time of adoption of this Code, shall be considered as continuations thereof and not as new enactments. 
Sec. 1-11. - Prior offenses, penalties, contracts or rights not affected by adoption of Code. 
(a)  Nothing in this Code or the ordinance adopting this Code shall affect any offense or act committed or done or any penalty or forfeiture incurred or any contract or right established or accruing before the effective date of this Code. 
(b)  The adoption of this Code shall not be interpreted as authorizing or permitting any use or the continuance of any use of a structure or premises in violation of any city ordinance in effect on the date of adoption of this Code. 
Sec. 1-12. - Certain ordinances not affected by Code. 
Nothing in this Code or the ordinance adopting this Code affects the validity of any the following ordinances or portions of ordinances, which ordinances or portions of ordinances continue in full force and effect to the same extent as if published at length in this Code: 
(1)  Amending the city Charter. 
(2)  Annexing property into the city or describing the corporate limits. 
(3)  Deannexing property or excluding property from the city. 
(4)  Promising or guaranteeing the payment of money or authorizing the issuance of bonds or other instruments of indebtedness. 
(5)  Authorizing or approving any contract, deed, or agreement. 
(6)  Granting any right or franchise. 
(7)  Making or approving any appropriation or budget. 
(8)  Providing for salaries or other employee benefits not codified in this Code. 
(9)  Adopting or amending the comprehensive plan. 
(10)  Levying or imposing any special assessment. 
(11)  Dedicating, establishing, naming, locating, relocating, opening, paving, widening, repairing or vacating any street, sidewalk or alley. 
(12)  Dedicating, accepting or vacating any plat or subdivision. 
(13)  Levying, imposing or otherwise relating to taxes not codified in this Code. 
(14)  Pertain to zoning, including but not limited to the basic zoning ordinance and ordinances rezoning property or amending the zoning map. 
(15)  That is temporary, although general in effect. 
(16)  That is special, although permanent in effect. 
(17)  The purpose of which has been accomplished. 
Chapter 2 - ADMINISTRATION[1]

All city buildings will be deemed smoke free. 
(Code 1977, § 2-4)

ARTICLE II. - CITY COUNCIL 

Sec. 2-31. - Time and days of meetings. 
The city council shall meet every first Tuesday of each month at 7:00 p.m. 
(Code 1977, § 2-1) 
Charter reference— Authority to fix time of meetings, § 12. 
Sec. 2-32. - Copies of minutes. 
A copy of the minutes of the meetings of the city council shall be mailed or delivered by the city clerk to each councilmember in sufficient time for such councilmember to receive the minutes prior to the next regular meeting. 
(Code 1977, § 2-3) 
Sec. 2-33. - Compensation. 
The mayor shall receive a salary of $500.00 per month. Councilmembers shall receive a salary of $150.00 per month.

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 2-181. - Designation of city depository; liability of officers and employees for funds. 
(a)  Such bank as is determined by the city council shall be designated as depository for such funds as may come into the hands of the city officers and employees, which funds shall be deposited in such bank. 
(b)  City officers and employees shall be held liable for all funds that may come into their hands while acting in their official capacities, until such funds are so deposited and receipts taken therefor. 
(Code 1977, § 9-1) 
Sec. 2-182. - Writing and signing checks. 
The city clerk shall have authority to write and sign all checks, which must also be signed by the mayor. 
(Code 1977, § 9-5) 
Sec. 2-183. - Approval of checks and accounts. 
All checks drawn and accounts paid by the city clerk that are of a legal and binding obligation of the city shall be approved. 
(Code 1977, § 9-6) 
Sec. 2-184. - Service charge on returned checks. 
The city will charge the maximum amount authorized by law as a service charge for handling each returned check. 
(Code 1977, § 9-8) 
State Law reference— Service charge limitations, O.C.G.A. § 16-9-20(j).

DIVISION 2. - PURCHASES AND EXPENDITURES[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference— Local government public works contracts, O.C.G.A. § 36-91-1 et seq. 

Sec. 2-211. - Bill approval and payment procedure. 
(a)  All purchases of every nature or kind for and on behalf of the city shall be made by a member of the city council or other officer or employee designated as purchasing agent. 
(b)  No bills, charges or debits shall be submitted to the city council for approval unless the bills, charges or debits bear the written approval of the purchasing agent. 
(c)  All bills against the city shall be submitted to the city council at its regular meeting and shall not be paid until so approved by the city council at its regular meeting. Only those bills contracted, authorized and approved by the purchasing agent shall be submitted to the city council for its approval. 
(Code 1977, § 9-2) 
Sec. 2-212. - Purchase order required for merchandise. 
A bill to the city will not be honored unless, when the merchandise was purchased, it was accompanied by a purchase order, signed by authorized personnel. 
(Code 1977, § 9-3) 
Sec. 2-213. - Purchases without council approval. 
The limits of purchases without council approval shall be $1,000.00 for the mayor and $100.00 for the city administrator. 
(Code 1977, § 9-4) 
Chapters 3—5 - RESERVED 
Chapter 6 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted April 7, 2015, amended ch. 6 in its entirety, in effect repealing and reenacting said chapter to read as set out herein. The former ch. 6, §§ 6-1, 6-2, 6-31—6-34, 6-61, 6-62, 6-91—6-96, 6-126—6-132, 6-161—6-167, 6-196—6-199, and 6-226—2-230, pertained to similar subject matter and derived from §§ 3-1—3-10, 3-21—3-28, 3-35—3-41, 3-42—3-48, 3-55—3-58, 3-58.1, 3-59, 3-59.1, 3-60, and 3-60.1—3-60.3 of the 1997 Code and Ord. No. 2007-01, adopted Nov. 6, 2007. 
Cross reference— Businesses, ch. 18; drinking in public, § 38-1; alcoholic beverages in parks, § 42-28. 
State Law reference— Alcoholic beverages, O.C.G.A. § 3-1-1 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 6-1. - Purpose of chapter and applicability of article. 
This chapter is enacted in furtherance of the police powers of the city to promote the health and general welfare of its citizens; to regulate and control the licensing and sale by the package and by the drink of beer, malt beverages, wine and distilled spirits; to establish reasonable regulations and ascertainable standards for licensees which will ensure the public peace; to protect schools, churches, residential areas from the negative secondary effects attributable to establishments that sell beer, malt beverages, wine and distilled spirits; and to ensure that only qualified persons obtain licenses for the manufacture, sale or distribution of beer, malt beverages, wine and distilled spirits. Further, unless otherwise provided, sections 6-2 through 6-27 of this article shall apply to all types of alcoholic beverage licenses issued by the city. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-2. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Alcohol means ethyl alcohol, hydrated oxide of ethyl, or spirits of wine, from whatever source or by whatever process produced. 
Alcoholic beverage means and includes all alcohol, distilled spirits, beer, malt beverage, wine or fortified wine. 
Beer or malt beverage means any alcoholic beverage obtained by the fermentation of any infusion or decoction of barley, malt, hops, or any other product, or any combination of such products in water, containing not more than six percent alcohol by volume, and including ale, porter, brown, stout, lager beer, small beer, and strong beer. The term "malt beverage" does not include sake, known as Japanese rice wine. 
Brown bag establishment means any restaurant, music hall, theater, or other establishment providing food or entertainment in the normal course of business, and in which the owners or their agents knowingly allow patrons to bring in and consume the patron's own alcoholic beverages. 
Code means the Code of Ordinances of the City of Lyons, Georgia. 
City means the City of Lyons, Georgia, and the land within the corporate limits of Lyons, Georgia within Toombs County, Georgia. 
Distilled spirits means any alcoholic beverage obtained by distillation or containing more than 21 percent alcohol by volume including, but not limited to, all fortified wines. 
Fortified wine means any alcoholic beverage containing more than 21 percent alcohol by volume made from fruits, berries, or grapes, either by natural fermentation or by natural fermentation with brandy added. The term "fortified wine" includes, but is not limited to, brandy. 
Governing authority means the city council of the City of Lyons, Georgia. 
Hotel means any lodge, inn, or similar establishment which offers overnight sleeping accommodations to registered guests for hire, and at which prepared meals or food are regularly served daily and consumed in one or more dining rooms, having an adequate and sanitary kitchen, such sleeping accommodations and dining rooms being conducted on the same premises. Hotels may grant franchises for the operation of a restaurant and lounge on their premises, and the holder of such franchise shall be included in this definition of a hotel. Lounges may be located separately from dining facilities in hotels provided there is a commonality of ownership of the restaurant and lounge. 
License means the authorization granted by the governing authority of the city to engage in the sale of alcoholic beverages in a specified manner for a calendar year, or the remaining portion of a calendar year. 
Licensee means the person to whom a license is issued or, in the case of any type of partnership, limited liability company or corporation, all partners, officers, managers and directors of the partnership, limited liability company or corporation, and the use of a masculine, feminine or neutral pronoun to describe licensee will contemplate the correct licensee even if the incorrect pronoun is used. 
Liter means metric measurement, currently used by the United States. 
Manager means the person who supervises the regular operations of businesses licensed under this chapter. 
Manufacturer means any maker, producer, or bottler of an alcoholic beverage. The word "manufacturer" also means: 
(1)  In the case of distilled spirits, any person engaged in distilling, rectifying, or blending any distilled spirits. 
(2)  In the case of malt beverages, any brewer. 
Minor means any person under the age of 21 years. 
Owner means any person or partner or stockholder or member owning any percentage of a business. 
Package means a bottle, can, keg, barrel or other original consumer container. 
Person means any individual, firm, partnership, cooperative, nonprofit corporation, joint venture, association, company, corporation, limited liability company, agency, syndicate, estate, trust, business trust, receiver, fiduciary, or other group or combination acting as a unit, body politic, or political subdivision, whether public, private or quasi-public. 
Premises means the space or area owned, leased or controlled by the licensee and used by the licensee for the purpose of operating under the license including any public sidewalk or roadway adjacent to the premises which is used by the licensee to sell alcoholic beverages. 
Public club means an establishment, other than a restaurant as defined in this chapter, having the principal purpose of offering live music, dancing, theatrical productions or comedians, and at which the consumption of alcoholic beverages on the premises only is an attendant purpose. A public club shall not be operated or conducted in conjunction with any other type of business, trade or profession and may offer and sale only those items commonly associated with such establishments. 
Public place means any place that the public is invited or permitted to go or congregate. 
Purchaser means and includes any individual, partnership, corporation, limited liability company, trust or association purchasing alcoholic beverages from a licensee. 
Restaurant means any public place used, maintained, advertised and held out to the public as a place where meals are actually and regularly served, without sleeping accommodations, such place being provided with adequate and sanitary kitchen, where the principal business is the sale of food, and that: (i) fills 75 percent of the usable square footage of its primary premises, including decks and patios which are immediately adjacent to and a part of its primary premises, with tables and chairs intended for dining, (ii) is staffed at all times while open to the public with a sufficient number and kind of employees to prepare, cook, and serve edible food to its guests, iii) is open to the public at least four hours a day, serving at least one meal per day, (iv) serves meals at least five days a week with the exception of weeks including holidays, vacations and periods of maintenance, construction or remodeling, (v) does not have a common table or counter area that comprises more than 25 percent of its dining area, and (vi) derives at least 51 percent of its total annual gross sales from the sale of prepared meals and food, and in calculating annual gross sales, it shall use all of its receipts, including those of persons laboring on the premises, such as all employees independent contractors, performers, servers and entertainers. 
Retail dealer means any person who sells alcoholic beverages, either in unbroken packages or for consumption on the premises, at retail only, to consumers and not for resale. 
School means any school building, school grounds, college campus, educational facility or educational building owned or run by or affiliated with a state, county, city or private or religious entity, any church school, day care, or kindergarten and to any building at such other schools in which are taught subjects commonly taught in the common schools and colleges of this state. It shall not apply to home schools. 
Wholesaler or wholesale dealer means any person who sells alcoholic beverages to other wholesale dealers, to retail dealers, or to retail consumption dealers. 
Wine means any alcoholic beverage containing not more than 21 percent alcohol by volume made from fruits, berries, or grapes, either by natural fermentation or by natural fermentation with brandy added. The term "wine" includes, but is not limited to, all sparkling wines, champagnes, combinations of such beverages, vermouths, special natural wines, rectified wines and like products. The term "wine" does not include cooking wine mixed with salt or other ingredients so as to render it unfit for human consumption as a beverage. A liquid shall first be deemed to be a wine at that point in the manufacturing process when it conforms to the definition of wine contained in this section. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 6-3. - Penalty for violation of chapter. 
It is unlawful for any person intentionally to violate any prohibition in this chapter. Any person who intentionally violates any provision of this chapter shall, after trial and conviction in the municipal court, be punished as provided in section 1-7 of this Code. Violation of any provision of this chapter may also, in addition to any criminal punishment, be cause for the denial, probation, suspension or revocation of any license issued hereunder. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-4. - License application and fees. 
(a)  Any person seeking any license permitted by this chapter shall file a written application with the city clerk, on the forms prescribed by the city clerk. Each application shall state: 
(1)  The applicant's full name, birth date, present address and addresses for the past five years, business address and business addresses of employers and their addresses for the last five years, name of spouse, complete record of all arrests, convictions and guilty pleas ("guilty plea", whenever used in this chapter, shall include any plea entered under any local, state or federal ordinance or law relating to nolo contendere, first offender or conditional discharge, regardless of the nomenclature used by the local, state or federal government) for violations of any city or local ordinance and of any state or federal law and the disposition of all arrests and charges within the last five years prior to the application. As well, the applicant shall present to the city clerk originals of the following documents for copying (such copies shall be kept by the city clerk): (i) current state driver's license, (ii) birth or naturalization certificate, and (iii) two forms of valid picture identification, including but not limited to current state driver's license, current passport, current state identification card or military identification card; 
(2)  Exact location of the applicant's proposed premises, including street address, zoning district and tax map and parcel number; 
(3)  Name and address of the owner or landlord and/or resident manager of the applicant's proposed premises, whether or not there is a building already erected thereon; 
(4)  Trade name (or proposed trade name) of the applicant's proposed business and/or premises; and 
(5)  Names and addresses of all persons having any financial or beneficial interest in the applicant's proposed business or premises. 
(b)  As to the manager of the applicant's proposed premises (if not the same as the applicant), the same information as required of the applicant in this section. 
(c)  Each application for a license under this chapter shall be accompanied by a certified bank check for the full amount of the license fee, together with a separate certified bank check in the amount of $200.00 to defray investigative and administrative costs. If the applicant withdraws his application prior to its being submitted to the city council, or if the application is denied by the city council, the deposit representing the license fee shall be refunded, but the $200.00 paid for investigation and administrative costs shall not be refunded. 
(d)  The application shall be sworn to or affirmed under oath. 
(e)  Surveyor's certificate. All new applications shall be accompanied by a current certificate from a registered surveyor containing the following information about the applicant's premises or proposed premises: 
(1)  A scale drawing of the premises or proposed premises, as situated on the proposed lot or land; 
(2)  Any proposed off-street parking facilities available to the premises or proposed premises and all outdoor lighting for the premises or proposed premises; 
(3)  The exact location of the premises or proposed premises, including street address and Toombs County tax map parcel number; 
(4)  Current zoning classification of the premises or proposed premises; and 
(5)  The distance in yards as measured in a straight line from the nearest property line of the premises or proposed premises to nearest property line of each of the following: the nearest school ground or college campus, the nearest church building and the nearest alcoholic treatment center which is owned and operated by the state or any county or municipal government. 
(f)  If the applicant's business has been licensed since July 1, 1981, or before, the survey shall be required however no license will be denied based upon a failure to meet the distance requirements as set forth under O.C.G.A. § 3-3-21. 
(g)  False information. An application under this chapter containing known false information may result in the denial of the license applied for and prosecution as a felony. 
(h)  As a prerequisite to the issuance of any such initial license only, the applicant shall furnish a complete set of fingerprints to be forwarded to the Georgia Bureau of Investigation, which shall search the files of the Georgia Crime Information Center for any instance of criminal activity during the two years immediately preceding the date of the application. The Georgia Bureau of Investigation shall also submit the fingerprints to the Federal Bureau of Investigation under the rules established by the United States Department of Justice for processing and identification of records. The federal record, if any, shall be obtained and returned to the governing authority submitting the fingerprints. 
(i)  Applications must be filed on or before November 30 of each year; otherwise, a penalty equal to 20 percent of the annual license fee shall be imposed. 
(j)  Except for temporary licenses that may be granted pursuant to this chapter, all licenses shall be for the full calendar year or for the number of months remaining in the calendar year. License fees shall not be prorated for any reason, and license fees shall not be refundable for any reason. 
(k)  Failure to furnish complete information in the application will delay the issuance of the license. The failure to furnish complete information within 30 days after being requested to do so by the city clerk may be cause to deny the application. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-5. - Moral character of license applicants. 
No person shall be issued any license unless it appears to the satisfaction of the city council that the license applicant is of good moral character. At the time an application is filed, the applicant shall, by affidavit duly sworn or affirmed, certify that he has not been convicted of or entered a guilty plea to any misdemeanor or felony involving moral turpitude, any lottery or gambling offense, or any offense related to illegal possession, distribution or sale of any illegal drug or substance (including but not limited to marijuana or any narcotic) or liquor within five years of the filing of the application. No license shall be granted where any applicant has been convicted under any federal, state, or local law or entered a guilty plea to any misdemeanor or felony involving moral turpitude, any lottery or gambling offense, or any offense related to illegal possession, distribution or sale of any illegal drug or substance (including but not limited to marijuana or any narcotic) or liquor within five years of the filing of the application. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-6. - General licensing qualifications. 
(a)  No applicant for a license shall be issued to any person who is not a citizen of the United States. In particular, no license for the retail sale of alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises only or for the retail sale of distilled spirits by the package shall be granted to any person who is has not been a resident of Toombs County, Georgia, for one year before the filing of the application, unless the applicant designates a Toombs County resident (such resident shall be an individual) who consents in writing to be responsible for any matter related to the license. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to sell, or possess for the purpose of sale, or offer to sell any alcoholic beverage within the city, except pursuant to a license as permitted by this chapter. 
(c)  An applicant shall possess a valid state alcohol or alcoholic beverage license before applying for a license as permitted by this chapter. 
(d)  A retail premises or business shall not have alcoholic beverages on its sales floor or in its cooler unless such premises or business has a license as permitted by this chapter. 
(e)  Any license issued under this chapter shall be a mere grant or privilege to carry on the business during the term of the license subject to all terms and conditions imposed by this chapter and state law. 
(f)  Where the applicant is any type entity, including but not limited to a partnership, limited liability company or corporation, the provisions of this section shall apply to all its partners, officers, members, managers. In the case of a corporation, the license shall be issued jointly to the corporation and its president or chief executive officer. In the case of limited liability company, the license shall be issued jointly to the company and to the holder of the largest economic interest in the company. In the case of a partnership, the license will be issued jointly to the partners. 
(g)  No license shall be issued to any person that has not attained the age of 21 years. 
(h)  No license shall be issued to any person who has had any license issued by the city revoked within the two years prior to the filing of an application as permitted by this chapter. 
(i)  The city council may decline to issue a license to any person that has violated any part of this chapter within one year prior to the filing of the application for such license. 
(j)  The city council may decline to issue a license where any person having any interest in or control over the licensee or licensed business or premises does not meet the same moral character requirements applicable to licensee, as set forth in this chapter. 
(k)  The city council may decline to issue a license when after reasonable effort the city clerk or chief of police is unable to verify any statement or information required to be disclosed in the application. 
(l)  Any person who is issued a license shall have and continuously maintain in Toombs County a registered agent upon whom any process, notice or demand required or permitted by law or under this chapter may be served upon. This registered agent shall be a resident of Toombs County. The licensee shall file the name of the registered agent, along with the written consent of such agent to receive any process, notice or demand required or permitted by law or under this chapter, with the city in such form as prescribed by the city clerk. 
(m)  No license shall be issued to any person until he provides the city clerk with proof of current commercial general liability insurance, covering the business and/or premises seeking the license, in the form of a true and correct insurance declarations page. Such proof must be provided annually to the city clerk. 
(n)  No license shall be issued to any person for the retail sale of alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises only or for the retail sale of distilled spirits by the package unless such person personally appears before the city council at one regularly scheduled council meeting. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-7. - Each location to have a separate license; transferability of license; fee required to change business owner, manager, partner, shareholder or business name. 
(a)  An applicant who will operate more than one premises shall complete a separate application for each premises and shall pay all applicable license fees for each premises. Each application shall be accompanied by a survey from a registered land surveyor showing that the premises is not within the prohibited distance from any school, school ground, church building or alcoholic treatment center owned and operated by the state or any county or municipal government. 
(b)  Each license shall be personal to the licensee. No license shall be transferable, except as provided in this section. 
(c)  In the case of the death of a licensee, the deceased licensee's license shall be the property of his, her, or its heirs or personal representatives, as the case may be, and the business or premises may continue to sell alcoholic beverages for a period of 45 days from the date of death of deceased licensee or until expiration of deceased licensee's license or until issuance of a new licensee, whichever occurs first, and upon such occurrence authorization to sell under the deceased licensee's license shall terminate by operation of law. 
(d)  If 50 percent or more of a licensed entity is to be sold or transferred to a person other than any existing partner, shareholder or member, then such licensed entity shall apply for a new license as set forth herein and pay all license costs and fees, if such licensed entity desires to be authorized, or continue to be authorized, to sell alcoholic beverages as permitted in this chapter. 
(e)  Any licensee who desires to change the location of his premises within the city shall so notify the city clerk in writing three business days prior to any such change of location. The notice of change of location shall be accompanied by a survey as required by subsection (a) of this section. A licensee's business shall not change location unless the new location complies with all provisions of this chapter. The city council shall have the authority to approve or deny the change of location in the same manner that it may approve or deny the issuance of a new license. An investigative fee of $200.00 shall be paid by the licensee at the time that a notice of change of location is made. If a change of location is approved, with no change of ownership of the business, the license fee paid for the old location shall be applied to the new location. 
(f)  Any licensee who desires to change the name of his business or premises shall so notify the city clerk in writing at least three business days prior to any change of name, and the city clerk shall direct the issuance of a corrected license in replacement of the original license. A fee of $25.00 shall be paid by the licensee at the time that such notice given for the change of name of such business or premises. 
(g)  Any licensee who changes the manager of his business or premises shall so notify the city clerk in writing at least three days of the effective date of notice of the change of manager and shall file with the city clerk such information about the new manager as the city clerk may require. A fee of $25.00 shall be paid at the time that the notice for the change of manager is made to defer the costs of investigation and administration. 
(h)  Except as provided in this section, any change in the ownership or control of any licensed entity shall be cause to revoke any license issued under this chapter. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-8. - Issuance of licenses subject to state law and code requirements. 
(a)  No license shall be issued to any elected official of the city or any employee of the city, nor shall any such person have any whole, partial or beneficial interest in any license. 
(b)  No license shall be issued in connection with any premises that fail to meet all applicable state and local fire, life safety, building, health, and zoning regulations of the Code. 
(c)  No license shall be issued in connection with any premises in any city zoning district, except for commercial zoning districts within the city known as C-1 and C-2. 
(d)  No license shall be issued to any applicant who is delinquent in the payment of city taxes or fees, including, but not limited to, property taxes, alcoholic beverage excise taxes, business license fees, occupational taxes, or any other tax or fee which is owed to the city by the applicant. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-9. - License may issue; sales prohibited in incomplete premises. 
Where a person applies for a license in connection with a premises that is not yet in existence or completed, a license may be issued for such premises, provided that the plans for such premises comply with this chapter and the Code. No sales shall be allowed in such premises until it has been completed in accordance with such plans, a certificate of occupancy issued, and it has been inspected by the proper officials, including but not limited to the city code enforcement officer, to ensure compliance with this chapter and the Code. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-10. - Expiration of license for failure to commence or operate business. 
(a)  All licensed premises must open for business within six months after issuance of the license. Failure to do so shall serve as a basis for revocation of such license by the city council, unless an extension of time is granted by the city manager before the expiration of the six-month period, for good cause shown by the licensee. No refund of the license fee shall be made in the event of a revocation hereunder. 
(b)  Any licensee who begins operating the business or premises authorized in the license, but who thereafter ceases operation for six months within any calendar year, shall be subject to revocation of his license by the city council, unless an extension of time is granted by the city manager before the expiration of the six-month period, for good cause shown by the licensee. No refund of license fee shall be made in the event of a revocation hereunder. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-11. - Expiration and renewal. 
(a)  All licenses shall expire on December 31 of each year. A licensee who desires to renew the license shall file an application, with the requisite fees as set forth in this chapter, with the city clerk on the form provided for renewal of the license for the ensuing year. All applications for renewal will be reviewed by the city clerk. A licensee does not have a right to automatic renewal and must be compliant with this chapter when applying for the renewal of his license. Applications for renewal must be filed on or before November 30 of each year; otherwise, a penalty equal to 20 percent of the annual license fee shall be imposed. No renewal license shall be granted after December 31, but such application shall be treated as an initial application, and the applicant shall be required to comply with all rules and regulations for the granting of licenses as if no previous license had been issued to licensee. 
(b)  Except for temporary licenses that may be granted pursuant to this chapter, all licenses granted under this chapter shall be for the full calendar year or for the number of months remaining in the calendar year. License fees shall not be prorated for any reason, and license fees shall not be refundable for any reason. 
(c)  Failure to furnish complete information in the renewal application will delay the issuance of the license. The failure to furnish complete information within 30 days after being requested to do so by the city clerk may be cause to deny the renewal application. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-12. - Denial, probation, suspension and revocation of licenses. 
(a)  Unless otherwise permitted in this chapter, no license which has been issued or which may be issued pursuant to this chapter shall be subjected to denial, probation, suspension or revocation, except for any ground, cause, good cause or due cause as hereinafter defined. 
(b)  The terms "ground", "cause", "good cause" or "due cause" (hereafter these terms may be collectively referred to as "ground") for the purposes of this section shall include, but not be limited to: 
(1)  Conviction of or guilty plea to any misdemeanor or felony involving moral turpitude, any lottery or gambling offense, or any offense related to illegal possession, distribution or sale of any illegal drug or substance (including but not limited to marijuana or any narcotic) or liquor, by the licensee or any of licensee's employees or any person holding an interest in the license; 
(2)  Knowing falsification of any fact given in an application for a license or bearing upon the licensee's qualification for a license; 
(3)  Failure or refusal to meet or maintain any requirement or standard prescribed by this chapter as a condition to or qualification for the issuance of a license; 
(4)  Violation of the specified days or hours of operation or sales as set out in this chapter; 
(5)  Selling or dispensing alcoholic beverages during a period of suspension; 
(6)  Where the licensee's business or premises does not meet the licensing requirements as set forth in this chapter; 
(7)  Littering, loitering or public consumption of alcoholic beverages in the area of the licensed business or premises; and 
(8)  Any other factor known to or discovered by the city council whereby it is objectively shown that the licensee, any of the licensee's employees or any person holding any interest in a license, has engaged in conduct at or involving the licensed business or premises, or has permitted conduct on the licensed premises, that constitutes a violation of federal or state law, local ordinance or administrative regulations involving alcoholic beverages, gambling or narcotics. With respect to this section, it may be inferred that the violative act was done with the knowledge or consent of the licensee; provided, however, that such inference may be rebutted only by evidence which precludes every other reasonable hypothesis save that such licensee did not know, assist or aid in such occurrence, or in the exercise of full diligence, could not have discovered or prevented such activity. 
(c)  The city council shall provide a written statement of charges of any ground, cause, good cause or due cause, to applicant or licensee, as the case may be, and the city council shall provide the statement of charges by personal service or by certified mail, return receipt requested, to the licensee or applicant and his attorney, if he is represented by an attorney, with a copy to the city attorney. Thereafter, the applicant or licensee shall have the right to request, within ten days of the date of the licensee's or applicant's receipt of the statement of charges, a hearing on the statement of charges, and he shall do so by filing a written hearing request with the city clerk. Upon receipt by the city clerk of the hearing request, a hearing shall be scheduled within 20 days, and the applicant or licensee shall be notified in writing, no less than five days before such hearing, of the date, time, and place of said hearing (the city's notice of hearing shall be served by personal service or certified mail, return receipt requested, to the licensee or applicant and his attorney, if he is represented by an attorney). The hearing shall be before the city council, and at the hearing the applicant or licensee shall have the right to appear in person and by attorney and to have witnesses appear on his behalf and to cross examine opposing witnesses and present evidence. The witnesses shall testify under oath, but technical rules of evidence shall not apply. 
(d)  In the event that the city council determines that there exists any ground for the suspension of a license, a period of license suspension may be imposed by the city council for a term not to exceed 90 days. In addition to such suspension, the city council is authorized to impose such special conditions as may be deemed necessary or appropriate by the city council. Such special conditions shall be designed to address or remedy the situation or circumstances that caused the imposition of the suspension. The city council must receive written certification of compliance with the special conditions by the chief of police in order to conclude suspension period, and in the event that the licensee fails to comply with the special conditions, then the license shall remain suspended until the chief of police provides the certification of compliance to the city council. 
(e)  In the event that the city council determines that there exists any ground for the revocation of a license, the revocation of a license by the city council shall be for the remaining calendar year of the year in which the revocation is imposed. In addition to such revocation, the city council is authorized to impose such special conditions as may be deemed necessary or appropriate by the city council with respect to the licensee reacquiring license. Such special conditions shall be designed to address or remedy the situation or circumstances that caused the imposition of the revocation. The city council must receive written certification of compliance with the special conditions by the chief of police in order to conclude the revocation period, and in the event that the licensee fails to comply with the special conditions, then the license shall remain revoked after the chief of police provides the certification of compliance to the city council. 
(f)  In the event that the city council determines that there exists any ground for the placing any license on probation, such probation shall be for a period not to exceed 90 days. In imposing such probation, the city council is authorized to impose special conditions upon the license holder that are designed to address or remedy the situation or circumstances that caused the imposition of the probation. In no event shall the license holder be prohibited from exercising the privileges of a license holder during the term of probation, except to the extent that such special conditions may impose conditions upon the exercise of such privileges during the term of the probation. 
(g)  The city council's decision regarding denial of an application, or probation, suspension or revocation of a license, shall be personally served or mailed by certified mail, return receipt requested, to the applicant or licensee and his attorney, if he is represented by an attorney, with a copy to the city attorney, within ten business days of the close of the hearing. The decision of the city council shall constitute final action by the city, subject to review upon petition for certiorari to the superior court of Toombs County, Georgia. 
(h)  Upon the licensee's or applicant's receipt of any statement of charges by the city council, the licensee may waive its right to a hearing and consent to a sanction, as recommended by the city manager, in consultation with the chief of police. Any consent entered under this chapter shall be in the form of a written decree, executed by the licensee and the city and non-appealable. 
(i)  Notwithstanding anything in this chapter to the contrary, upon the revocation of a licensee's state alcohol or alcoholic beverage license, the licensee's license issued under this chapter shall be immediately revoked by operation of law. The chief of police, upon notice of this revocation, shall take the necessary steps to ensure the immediate cessation of such licensee's sale of alcoholic beverages. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-13. - Inspection of licensed business or premises by the police department. 
Sworn police officers of the city shall have the authority to inspect any business or premises licensed under this chapter during the hours in which the business or premises is open for business. These inspections shall be made for the purpose of verifying compliance with the requirements of this chapter and state law. This section is not intended to limit the authority of any other city officer to conduct inspections authorized by other provisions of this Code or state law. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-14. - License and certain code provisions to be posted. 
(a)  All licenses shall include a statement as to the type of license issued, the name of the licensee, the name of the licensed business or premises, and the address of the licensed business or premises. All licenses shall, at all times, be kept in plain view within the licensed business or premises. 
(b)  All licensees shall post in a prominent location on the licensed business or premises, in plain view of all individuals on the premises, an approved sign setting forth or summarizing the laws of the city and the state in regard to the sale of alcoholic beverages to underage or intoxicated persons. 
(c)  Each sign shall be of a size and configuration approved by the chief of police and include either the language of the applicable Code sections, or summaries approved by the chief of police. 
(d)  The city clerk is authorized to design and have printed approved signs, which shall be made available to licensees at a price, not to exceed $75.00, to be established by the city clerk and maintained as a public document by the city clerk. 
(e)  All licenses shall be a mere grant of privilege to carry on the business during the term of the license, subject to all terms and conditions imposed by the ordinances of the city and state law. 
(f)  All licenses shall have printed on the front these words: "THIS LICENSE IS A MERE PRIVILEGE SUBJECT TO BEING SUSPENDED OR REVOKED AND IS SUBJECT TO ANY FUTURE ORDINANCES WHICH MAY BE ENACTED." 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-15. - Application of chapter provisions to minors generally. 
(a)  No person under 18 years of age shall be employed in or about the premises of any person licensed to sell alcoholic beverages. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for a person under 21 years of age to attempt to purchase an alcoholic beverage or for any person to purchase an alcoholic beverage for a person under 21 years of age. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for a person under 21 years of age to exhibit faked, forged, or borrowed credentials in an effort to obtain an alcoholic beverage to which he is not legally entitled. 
(d)  It shall be unlawful for a person under 21 years of age, other than an employee employed by a licensed person, to have an open container of any alcoholic beverage in his possession. 
(e)  It shall be a violation for any licensee not to require and properly check identification to ensure that a person under 21 years of age is not sold, served, or has in his possession any alcoholic beverage while in a licensed business or premises, except that a licensed employee working in a licensed business or premises may have in his possession any alcoholic beverage for the purpose of selling or serving such alcoholic beverages. The term "identification" as used in this section, shall mean any document issued by a governmental agency containing a description of the person, a photograph, and giving such person's date of birth, and includes, without being limited to, a passport, military identification card, driver's license or state department of public safety identification card. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-16. - Acts prohibited by licensee generally. 
No licensee shall do any of the following upon the licensed business or premises: 
(1)  Sell or distribute any alcoholic beverage to a person under 21 years of age. 
(2)  Sell or distribute any alcoholic beverage to any person while such person is in an intoxicated condition. 
(3)  Sell or distribute any alcoholic beverage on any day or at any time when such sale is prohibited by law. 
(4)  Allow any person to consume any alcoholic beverage on the premises of a person not licensed for the retail sale of any alcoholic beverage by drink for consumption on the premises only. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-17. - Purchases from and sales to person other than licensees 
No licensed retail dealer shall purchase any alcoholic beverage from any person other than a licensed wholesale dealer. No licensed wholesale dealer shall sell any alcoholic beverages to any person other than a licensed retail dealer. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-18. - Unlawful conduct on licensed premises. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for a licensee, his agent or employee to permit any disturbance of the peace, any obscenity, or any lewd, immoral or improper behavior, conduct or practices in the licensed business or premises, or to operate the licensed business or premises in such a manner as to create a nuisance. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any licensee, his agent or employee to fail to report to the police department any disturbance which occurs immediately outside his business or premises, or in the parking facilities of his business or premises, of which he has knowledge. 
(c)  It shall be the duty and responsibility of the licensee, his agent, or employee to report to the police department any usage or possession of illegal drugs or narcotics and to report any unlawful conduct of any nature which occurs on the licensed premises, of which he has knowledge. 
(d)  It shall be unlawful for any licensee, his agent or employee, to fail to assist any law enforcement officer in the performance of the officer's duties while the officer is in or on a licensed business or premises. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-19. - Open area and patio sales. 
Consumption or sale of alcoholic beverages in open areas or on decks or patios is not permitted unless a licensee's business or premises is licensed for the retail sale of alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises only, and such licensee complies with the following regulations: 
(1)  The open area, patio or deck must be enclosed in a manner that directs ingress and egress by the public through a single entrance only through the licensed business or premises. The purpose of this requirement is to prevent a customer from leaving the open area, patio or deck with an alcoholic beverage without the licensee's knowledge. 
(2)  The open area, patio or deck shall be enclosed by a structure at least 42 inches in height as measured from the floor of the open area, patio or deck. Such structure must meet all building code requirements of the city. 
(3)  Any licensee desiring to obtain approval for open area, patio or deck sales must submit to the city a complete set of plans that will be reviewed and approved on an individual basis by appropriate city employee(s). All plans and final construction pursuant to such plans shall meet the requirements of this chapter, all applicable health, life safety and fire codes, any other code applicable to such structures. Only upon satisfactory completion of all final inspections will the city approve of any open area, patio or deck sales. 
(4)  Any structure or area set aside for open area, patio or deck sales shall not contain a number of square feet that represents an amount greater than 40 percent of the existing seating area of the licensed business or premises. 
(5)  Loudspeakers or other amplifiers of sound shall not be permitted upon the open areas, patios or decks of any licensed business or premises. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-20. - Open containers and brown bag establishments prohibited. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to drink any alcoholic beverages or other intoxicating beverage at any public place within the city, or for any person to have in his possession any unsealed or opened container with such intoxicating beverage in it at any public place within the city, except as may be otherwise temporarily permitted by this chapter or the Code. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to drink or possess any alcoholic beverage upon real property of the city that is used as a public park, playground or school. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for any person to drink any alcoholic beverages in any automobile on the streets of the city, whether such automobile shall be moving or parked. 
(d)  Brown bag establishments shall be prohibited within the city. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
State Law reference— Local location restrictions, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-21(b)(3). 
Sec. 6-21. - Signs and advertising. 
(a)  No outdoor advertising promoting the sale or consumption of alcoholic beverages shall be permitted on the exterior of any business or premises that is licensed for wholesale or retail sale of alcoholic beverages or any business or premises that is licensed for the sale of alcoholic beverages for consumption on the premises only. 
(b)  Any indoor sign or display promoting the sale or consumption of alcoholic beverages may be visible from the exterior of any business or premises that is licensed for wholesale or retail sale of alcoholic beverages or any business or premises that is licensed for the sale of alcoholic beverages for consumption on the premises only, subject to the limitations of section 6-25. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-22. - Happy hour promotions. 
No licensee, or his agent or employee, shall engage in any of the following practices in connection with the sale or other disposition of alcoholic beverages for consumption on the premises: (a) advertising "Happy Hour" through any form of media, including, but not limited to, newspapers, magazines, electronics, radio, television and internet, or (b) outdoor advertising or signs promoting "Happy Hour" on the exterior of any licensed premises or on the windows or elsewhere on the licensed business or premises that may be viewed from the outside. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-23. - Measurement of distances. 
Unless otherwise provided by law, all measurements, to determine distances as required by this chapter relating to the issuance of alcoholic beverage licenses, shall be measured by the most direct route of travel on the ground and shall be measured in the following manner: 
(1)  From the front door of the structure in which alcoholic beverages are sold or offered for sale; 
(2)  In a straight line to the nearest public sidewalk, walkway, street, road or highway; 
(3)  Along such public sidewalk, walkway, street, road or highway by the nearest route; 
(4)  To the front door of the building (in the case of churches or alcoholic treatment centers which are owned and operated by the state or any county or municipal government), or to the nearest portion of the grounds (in the case of schools), whichever is more appropriate under the applicable section. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Cross reference— Zoning, app. A.
