State Law reference— Local location restrictions, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-21(b)(3). 
Sec. 6-24. - Hours of operation for licensees. 
(a)  A licensed retail dealer of alcoholic beverages by the package shall not sell, give away or otherwise distribute any alcoholic beverage during the following time periods: 
(1)  Monday: from 12:01 a.m. until 6:00 a.m.; 
(2)  Tuesday through Saturday: from 2:00 a.m. until 6:00 a.m.; and 
(3)  Sunday: from 12:01 a.m. until 12:30 p.m. and from 11:30 p.m. through 12:00 midnight; provided that, the sale of alcoholic beverages on Sunday under this subsection shall also be subject to and governed by section 6-28(a). 
(b)  A licensed retail dealer of alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises only shall not sell, give away or otherwise distribute any alcoholic beverage during the following time periods: 
(1)  Monday: from 12:01 a.m. until 10:00 a.m.; 
(2)  Tuesday through Saturday: from 2:00 a.m. until 10:00 a.m.; and 
(3)  Sunday: from 12:01 a.m. until 12:30 p.m.; provided that, the sale of alcoholic beverages on Sunday under this subsection shall also be subject to and governed by section 6-28(b). 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015; Ord. No. 1286, § I, 12-19-2017) 
State Law reference— Hours of sale, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-20; private clubs authorized to sell alcohol on Sundays, O.C.G.A. § 3-7-2; Sunday sales of wine at farm wineries, O.C.G.A. § 3-6-21.2. 
Sec. 6-25. - Visibility. 
(a)  The business or premises of each licensee shall have a clearly marked point(s) of entry. 
(b)  The business or premises of each licensee shall have point(s) of entry that are clearly visible from a public street; however, this requirement shall not apply to hotels or where the point of entry of the licensed business or premises is in a shopping center or business building. 
(c)  The business or premises of each licensee shall ensure that, at all points of entry, there are clear windows and doors. Further, the business or premises of each licensee must maintain clear windows and doors for any cashier's cage within the premises, or other internally enclosed space. 
(d)  The business or premises of each licensee, including those entirely enclosed in another building, such as a restaurant located in a hotel, must keep all windows and doors free of visual obstructions so that the interior of such business or premises is clearly visible from the exterior. No tinting, shades, curtains, blinds or other devices shall be used to obstruct the view into the such business or premises, but tinting, shades, curtains, blinds, and other devices may be used to reduce sun glare so long as such measures do not impede visual access to the business or premises. 
(e)  The business or premises of each licensee shall operate with an adequate level of internal lighting, so as to ensure visual access from the exterior and safety to law enforcement or other emergency responders, 24 hours, a day seven days a week. External lighting cannot be solely used to meet this requirement. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-26. - Completeness, denial and re-submittal of application. 
(a)  No license application shall be considered until the city clerk deems the same complete as set forth in this chapter. 
(b)  If the license application is denied, the same or substantially same license application cannot be resubmitted for a period of six months from the date of the denial. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-27. - Production of records; audits. 
(a)  In conjunction with any license application, or in conjunction with the issuance of any license, or in conjunction with the revocation, suspension or cancellation of any license, or in conjunction with the payment or nonpayment of any excise tax levied or to be collected under this chapter, the city clerk shall have the right to subpoena all or any part of the records, books, documents, electronic or magnetic media or documents and associated software, and reports or invoices in any form of any licensee for the purpose of auditing the records of such licensee, securing compliance by such licensee with the provisions of this chapter, proving or disproving any ground or any violation of any part of this chapter by any licensee, or showing payment or nonpayment of any taxes, fees or charges as contemplated by this chapter. 
(b)  All licensees shall maintain the following records for a period of three years from the issuance of any license and make the original records, or certified copies thereof, available to the city manager for audit at the licensed premises: 
(1)  Monthly income or operating statements; 
(2)  Daily sales receipts and invoices showing liquor, beer, malt beverages and wine separately; 
(3)  Daily cash register receipts; 
(4)  Monthly Georgia Sales and Use Tax Reports; and 
(5)  Federal Income Tax Returns with all Form 1099s. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-28. - Sunday sales licenses. 
(a)  A retail dealer of alcoholic beverages by the package may apply for and obtain a Sunday sales license for the retail sale of alcoholic beverages by the package upon due qualification for and payment for such license, as set forth in this chapter. 
(b)  A retail dealer of alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises only may apply for and obtain a Sunday sales license for the retail sale of alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises only, upon the occurrence of the following: (1) due qualification for and payment for such license, as set forth in this chapter; and (2) showing to the satisfaction of the city manager, or his designee, that such retail dealer derives at least 50 percent of its total annual gross sales from the sale of prepared meals or food in all of the combined retail outlets of the individual establishments where food is served and in any licensed establishment which derives at least 50 percent of its total annual gross income from the rental of rooms for overnight lodging. 
(Ord. No. 1286, § I, 12-19-2017) 
Secs. 6-29—6-49. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - BEER, MALT BEVERAGES AND WINE[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Beer, O.C.G.A. § 3-5-1 et seq.; wine, O.C.G.A. § 3-6-1 et seq. 

Sec. 6-50. - Authority to sell; license required. 
A license for a retail dealer or wholesale dealer for the sale of beer, malt beverages and/or wine may be granted by the city council upon the terms and conditions as provided in this article. Further, a license for the retail sale of beer, malt beverages and/or wine by the drink for consumption on the premises only may be granted by the city council upon the terms and conditions as provided in this article. No person will be issued a license for the sale of beer, malt beverages and/or wine, where the same is sold in the original packages, and a license for the sale of beer, malt beverages and/or wine by the drink for consumption on the premises only, at the same location. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-51. - License fees. 
Before any license permitted under this article is granted by the city council, the license applicant shall comply with all regulations adopted by the city council applicable to such licenses and pay the applicable license fee by certified bank check in an amount set by resolution or ordinance by the city council and maintained as a public document by the city clerk. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
State Law reference— Maximum license fee, O.C.G.A. § 3-4-50. 
Sec. 6-52. - Excise taxes on beer and malt beverages. 
(a)  There is hereby levied and imposed upon the sale of beer and malt beverages within the city, a specific excise tax as follows: 
(1)  Where beer and malt beverages are sold in or from a barrel or bulk container, a tax of $6.00 on each container sold containing not more than 15½ gallons and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of 15½ gallons; and 
(2)  Where beer and malt beverages are sold in bottles, cans, or other containers, except barrel or bulk containers, a tax of $0.05 per 12 ounces and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of 12 ounces. 
(b)  The excise taxes provided for in this section shall be imposed upon and shall be paid by the licensed wholesale dealer in beer and malt beverages. Each wholesale dealer selling beer and malt beverages within the city shall file a report with the city by the tenth day of each month showing for the preceding calendar month the exact quantities of beer and malt beverages, by size and type of container, sold during the month within the city. Each wholesale dealer shall remit to the city on the tenth day of the month after the calendar month in which such sales were made the amount of excise tax due in accordance with this section. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
State Law reference— Required municipal excise tax on beer, O.C.G.A. § 3-5-80. 
Sec. 6-53. - Excise taxes on wine. 
(a)  There is hereby levied and imposed upon the sale of wine within the city, a specific excise tax in the amount of $0.22 per liter and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of a liter. 
(b)  The taxes imposed by this section shall not be levied with respect to: 
(1)  Wine sold to and used by established and recognized churches and synagogues for use in sacramental services only; 
(2)  Any sale of wine which is exempt from taxation by the state under the Constitution of the United States; 
(3)  Wine sold to persons outside the state for resale or consumption outside the state; or 
(4)  Wine which contains less than one-half of one percent alcohol. 
(c)  The excise taxes as provided for in this section shall be imposed upon and paid by the licensed wholesale dealer in wine, and each wholesale dealer of wine within the city shall file a report with the clerk by the tenth day of each month showing for the preceding calendar month the exact quantities of wine, by size and type of container, sold during the month within the city. Each wholesale dealer shall remit to the city on the tenth day of the month after the calendar month in which such sales were made the amount of excise tax due in accordance with subsection (b) of section 6-52. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
State Law reference— Municipal excise tax on wine, O.C.G.A. § 3-6-60 et seq. 
Sec. 6-54. - Sale without license; separate application and separate license required for each premises. 
Beer, malt beverages and/or wine shall not be distributed, sold or possessed for the purposes of sale without a license granted by the city council. A separate application must be made, and a separate license must be obtained, to sell beer, malt beverages and/or wine for each premises where beer, malt beverages and/or wine is sold at retail or wholesale, or where beer, malt beverages and/or wine is sold at retail by the drink for consumption on the premises only. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-55. - Limitation regarding licenses for retail sale of beer, malt beverages and/or wine by the drink for consumption on the premises only. 
A license for the retail sale of beer, malt beverages and/or wine by the drink for consumption on the premises only shall be issued only in conjunction with a restaurant, hotel or public club and where a restaurant, hotel or public club is within the commercial zoning districts described in section 6-8. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-56. - Reporting requirements for restaurants. 
(a)  Where a license is issued for the retail sale of beer, malt beverages and/or wine by the drink for consumption on the premises only, in conjunction with a restaurant, the licensee of such license shall submit quarterly written reports to the city clerk, as more particularly set forth herein. 
(b)  Every report shall be post marked on or before the last day of the calendar month after the calendar quarter. 
(c)  Every report shall be in a form recognized and accepted by certified public accountants and shall utilize common and generally recognized accounting principles and shall be submitted under oath. False information in any report may result in the prosecution under O.C.G.A. § 16-10-20 by a court of competent jurisdiction. 
(d)  Every report shall clearly indicate all sales receipts of the restaurant for food and alcoholic beverages, and for reporting purposes, food shall be defined as all edible substances appropriate for human consumption as determined by the health department inspecting the city's restaurants as sold or provided to the public in a restaurant. Food shall not be construed to include olives, cherries, limes, lemons, salt, pepper, pineapples, celery, tomato juice, or any other fruit or vegetable, or any dairy product such as ice cream, cream, yogurt or milk, or any soft drink, water, tonic water or non-alcoholic carbonated or non-carbonated beverages, when such items are used in any alcoholic beverage or mixed drink as a essential part of the beverage, mixed drink, or as a garnish thereon. 
(e)  Notwithstanding anything in this chapter to the contrary, if any report of a restaurant shows that its sales receipts for food comprise less than 51 percent of a restaurant's total gross sales receipts in any quarter of a calendar year, then, thereafter, the city council may consider such event as cause for probation, suspension or revocation. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-57. - Proximity to church buildings, schools or school grounds. 
(a)  No license shall be issued under this article where the entrance to a place of business or premises for the wholesale sale of beer, malt beverages or wine is located within 100 yards of the entrance to any church building or the property line of any school or school grounds. 
(b)  No license shall be issued under this article where the entrance to a place of business or premises for the retail sale of beer, malt beverages or wine in original packages is located within 100 yards of the entrance to any church building or the property line of any school or school grounds. 
(c)  No license shall be issued under this article where the entrance to a place of business or premises for the retail sale of beer, malt beverages or wine by the drink for consumption on the premises only is located within 25 feet of the entrance to any church building or the property line of any school or school grounds. In this subsection, a church building is defined as a free-standing structure, originally built for use as a church, and a church building does not include a commercial or retail building or space that has been converted for occupancy by a church or for religious purposes. 
(d)  For the purposes of this section, distances shall be measured as provided in section 6-23. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
State Law reference— Location restrictions, O.C.G.A. § 3-3-21(b)(3). 
Sec. 6-58. - Wholesaler's delivery to licensed retail dealer; marking of vehicles. 
No beer, malt beverages and/or wine shall be delivered to any licensed retail dealer except by a licensed wholesale dealer, who shall make such deliveries by a vehicle owned by the wholesaler, with wholesaler's name clearly marked on the outside of the vehicle. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-59. - Machines operated for amusement purposes in licensed retail businesses. 
No person with a license for the retail sale of beer, malt beverages or wine shall permit on his premises any coin operated amusement machine, including but not limited to a slot machine, mechanical music box or pinball machine, or any form of electronic or mechanical game machine or coin-operated device, which might be used for entertainment or amusement purposes, except pursuant to applicable state law. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Secs. 6-60—6-69. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PACKAGED DISTILLED SPIRITS 

Sec. 6-70. - Authority to sell; license required. 
A license for the retail sale or wholesale sale of distilled spirits by the original package may be granted by the city council upon the terms and conditions as provided in this article. No person may hold a license for the sale of distilled spirits by the package and a license for the sale of distilled spirits by the drink for consumption on the premises only at the same location. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-71. - License fee; excise tax in addition to retail license fee. 
(a)  Before any license permitted under this article is granted by the city council, the license applicant shall comply with all regulations adopted by the city council applicable to such licenses and pay the applicable license fee by certified bank check in an amount set by resolution or ordinance by the city council and maintained as a public document by the city clerk. 
(b)  In addition to the license fees established by this section, there is hereby levied and imposed a specific excise tax on the sale of distilled spirits by the package within the city, in the amount of $0.22 per liter of distilled spirits, excluding fortified wine, and a proportionate tax at the same rate on all fractional parts of a liter. The excise tax as provided for in this section shall be imposed upon and shall be paid by the licensed wholesale dealer in distilled spirits by the package. The payment and filing of returns requirements of such wholesale dealer shall be as provided in subsection (b) of section 6-52. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-72. - Application for license to be accompanied by sworn statement regarding additional information. 
(a)  All applications for licenses under this article, both original and renewal, must be accompanied by a full and complete statement under oath of information describing any and all interests, as defined by state law, in the person licensed or to be licensed. This information shall include the names and addresses of any person who has any ownership interest in the person licensed or to be licensed and the size of such interest; the specific street address of any other premises which is authorized for retail sale of alcoholic beverages by the package in which the person licensed or to be licensed has any ownership interest; detailed description of the ownership or leasehold of premises where the person licensed or to be licensed is or will be operating, including but not limited to an executed copy of the vesting deed or lease; and the name and address of any owner and lessor of the premises in which the person licensed or to be licensed is or will be operating. 
(b)  Any change in the information required in subsection (a) must be filed with the city clerk when the change occurs, and failure to do so within a period of ten days if such change shall be grounds for denial, probation, suspension or revocation, as may apply, by the city council. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-73. - Proximity to church buildings, schools or school grounds. 
(a)  No license shall be issued under this article where an entrance to the place of business or premises for wholesale or retail sale of distilled spirits is located as follows: 
(1)  Within 100 yards of the entrance of any church building; or 
(2)  Within 200 yards of the property line of any school or school grounds. 
(b)  For the purposes of this section, distances shall be measured as provided in section 6-23. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-74. - Places where retail sales permitted. 
(a)  No distilled spirits by the package shall be sold at retail except in: 
(1)  Retail businesses or premises in which space has been set aside and devoted substantially to the retail sale of distilled spirits by the package, with ingress and egress provided directly to, and only to, the exterior of the buildings in which the business or premises is located and not any other enclosed part of the building in which such business or premises is located, except as provided hereafter. 
(2)  Hotels and office buildings where: 
a.  Every public entrance to such business or premises shall be from a lobby, hallway or other interior portion of the primary use structure; and 
b.  No show window, advertising or display shall be visible from the exterior of the primary use structure. 
(b)  Each license for the retail sale of distilled spirits by the package shall have conspicuously displayed within the interior of his business or premises not less than four copies of a printed price list of the distilled spirits offered for sale, provided that a licensee, in lieu of having four copies of a printed price list, may have the prices placed on the bottles or on the front of the shelf where distilled spirits are exhibited for sale. 
(c)  No exterior signs may be used to advertise the price of any distilled spirits offered for sale at the business or premises of a person licensed for retail sale of distilled spirits by the package. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-75. - Machines operated for amusement purposes in licensed retail businesses. 
No person with a license for the retail sale of distilled spirits by the package shall permit on his premises any coin operated amusement machine, including but not limited to a slot machine, mechanical music box or pinball machine, or any form of electronic or mechanical game machine or coin-operated device, which might be used for entertainment or amusement purposes, except pursuant to applicable state law. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-76. - Signs and display of license. 
(a)  Signs advertising or promoting the sale of distilled spirits by the package are permitted within the city, in accordance with this chapter and as otherwise permitted in the Code. 
(b)  The license for the retail sale of distilled spirits by the package shall be displayed on a front window or entrance of the licensed premises, with the name of the licensee, together with the inscription "City of Lyons License for Retail Sale of Distilled Spirits by the Package, No. _____," and the letters, numbers and symbols on the license shall be not less than four inches, nor more than eight inches, in height. 
(c)  The license shall at all times be kept in plain view within the licensed premises or business. 
Sec. 6-77. - Persons with financial interest in wholesale dealer license; wholesaler's delivery to licensed retail dealer; marking of vehicles. 
(a)  No person who has any financial interest in a wholesale dealer license for the sale of distilled spirits shall be issued any license for the retail sale of distilled spirits by the package. 
(b)  No distilled spirits shall be delivered to any licensed retail dealer in the city except by a licensed wholesale dealer, who shall make such deliveries by a vehicle owned by the wholesaler, with the wholesaler's name clearly marked on the outside of the vehicle. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Secs. 6-78—6-89. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - SALE OF DISTILLED SPIRITS BY THE DRINK FOR CONSUMPTION ON PREMISES ONLY 

Sec. 6-90. - Authority to sell; license required. 
A license for the retail sale of distilled spirits by the drink for consumption on the premises only may be granted by the city council, upon the terms and conditions as provided in this article. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-91. - License fees. 
Before any license permitted under this article is granted by the city council, the license applicant shall comply with all regulations adopted by the city council applicable to such license and pay the applicable license fee by certified bank check in an amount set by resolution or ordinance by the city council and maintained as a public document by the city clerk. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-92. - Separate application and separate license required for each premises. 
A separate application must be made, and a separate license must be obtained, for the retail sale of distilled spirits by the drink for consumption on the premises only for each premises where distilled spirits are sold at retail by the drink for consumption on the premises only. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-93. - Consumption sales only. 
Persons issued a license for retail sale of distilled spirits by the drink for consumption on the premises only shall not be licensed to sell distilled spirits by the package or bottle. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-94. - Limitation regarding licenses for retail sale of distilled spirits by the drink for consumption on premises only. 
A license for the retail sale of distilled spirits by the drink for consumption on the premises only shall be issued only in conjunction with a restaurant, hotel or public club and where the restaurant, hotel or public club is within the commercial zoning districts described in section 6-8. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-95. - Reporting requirements for restaurants. 
(a)  Where a license is issued for the retail sale of distilled spirits by the drink for consumption on the premises only, in conjunction with a restaurant, the licensee of such license shall submit quarterly written reports to the city clerk, as more particularly set forth herein. 
(b)  Every report shall be post marked on or before the last day of the calendar month after the calendar quarter. 
(c)  Every report shall be in a form recognized and accepted by certified public accountants and shall utilize common and generally recognized accounting principles and shall be submitted under oath. False information in any report may result in the prosecution under O.C.G.A. § 16-10-20 by a court of competent jurisdiction. 
(d)  Every report shall clearly indicate all sales receipts of the restaurant for food and alcoholic beverages, and for reporting purposes, food shall be defined as all edible substances appropriate for human consumption as determined by the health department inspecting the city's restaurants as sold or provided to the public in a restaurant. Food shall not be construed to include olives, cherries, limes, lemons, salt, pepper, pineapples, celery, tomato juice, or any other fruit or vegetable, or any dairy product such as ice cream, cream, yogurt or milk, or any soft drink, water, tonic water or non-alcoholic carbonated or non-carbonated beverages, when such items are used in any alcoholic beverage or mixed drink as a essential part of the beverage, mixed drink, or as a garnish thereon. 
(e)  Notwithstanding anything in this chapter to the contrary, if any report of a restaurant shows that its sales receipts for food comprise less than 51 percent of a restaurant's total gross sales receipts in any quarter of a calendar year, then, thereafter, the city council may consider such event as cause for probation, suspension or revocation. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-96. - Proximity to church buildings, schools or school grounds. 
(a)  No license shall be issued under this article where the entrance to a place of business or premises for the retail sale of distilled spirits by the drink for consumption on the premises only is located within 25 feet of the entrance to any church building or the property line of any school or school grounds. In this section, a church building is defined as a free-standing structure, originally built for use as a church, and a church building does not include a commercial or retail building or space that has been converted for occupancy by a church or for religious purposes. 
(b)  For the purposes of this section, distances shall be measured as provided in section 6-23. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-97. - Machines operated for amusement purposes in licensed retail businesses. 
No person with a license for the retail sale of distilled spirits by the drink for consumption on the premises only shall permit on his premises any coin operated amusement machine, including but not limited to a slot machine, mechanical music box or pinball machine, or any form of electronic or mechanical game machine or coin-operated device, which might be used for entertainment or amusement purposes, except pursuant to applicable state law. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Sec. 6-98. - Wholesaler's delivery to licensed retail dealer; marking of vehicles. 
No distilled spirits shall be delivered to any licensed retail dealer except by a licensed wholesale dealer, who shall make such deliveries by a vehicle owned by the wholesaler, with wholesaler's name clearly marked on the outside of the vehicle. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Secs. 6-99—6-109. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - TEMPORARY LICENSES 

Sec. 6-110. - Nonprofit corporations eligible for temporary licenses. 
A nonprofit corporation or organization may apply to the city council for a temporary license limited to the retail sale of wine, malt beverages and/or beer for consumption on the premises only. As a condition to the granting of the temporary license, the nonprofit corporation or organization shall provide written proof to the city clerk of its status as a duly authorized, operating and existing corporation or organization (such proof includes a valid certificate of incorporation from the Georgia Secretary of State and a certificate of 501(c)(3) status from the Internal Revenue Service). The nonprofit corporation or organization will comply with article I of this chapter, though it is not required to operate as a restaurant or public club, and no temporary license shall be granted for a period longer than three consecutive days or more than four times in any calendar year. Notwithstanding anything in this chapter to the contrary, each temporary license fee shall be $250.00. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Secs. 6-111—6-125. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - ANNUAL LICENSE FEES 

Sec. 6-126. - Establishment of annual license fees. 
(a)  There is hereby imposed an annual license fee, payable at the time of issuance of any license under this chapter and any renewal thereof, as follows: 
For wholesale dealers: 
Wholesale: Beer or malt beverages ..... $ 100.00 
Wholesale: Wine ..... 100.00 
Wholesale: Distilled spirits ..... 100.00 
For retail dealers: 
By the drink for consumption on the premises: Beer or malt beverages ..... 300.00 
By the drink for consumption on the premises: Wine ..... 300.00 
By the drink for consumption on the premises: Distilled spirits ..... 650.00 
By the drink for consumption on the premises on Sunday: Beer or malt beverages ..... 50.00 
By the drink for consumption on the premises on Sunday: Wine ..... 50.00 
By the drink for consumption on the premises on Sunday: Distilled spirits ..... 350.00 
Retail package: Beer or malt beverages ..... 150.00 
Retail package: Wine ..... 150.00 
Retail package: Distilled spirits ..... 3,000.00 
Retail package on Sunday: Beer or malt beverages ..... 0.00 
Retail package on Sunday: Wine ..... 0.00 
Retail package on Sunday: Distilled spirits ..... 0.00 
(b)  The license fees imposed by this section are regulatory fees intended to offset the city's cost in administering and enforcing this chapter. In addition thereto, licensees are subject to payment of any occupational tax as set forth in this Code. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015; Ord. No. 1286, § II, 12-19-2017) 
Secs. 6-127—6-150. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - EXEMPTIONS 

Sec. 6-151. - Grandfather clause. 
Notwithstanding anything in this chapter to the contrary, the city council's enactment of this chapter will not revoke or suspend the existing license of a licensee who, as of the date of the enactment of this chapter, holds a license for retail sale of alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption on the premises only and whose business or premises may not qualify as a restaurant or public club under this chapter. However, except as provided herein, upon the city council's enactment of this chapter, any license issued pursuant to this chapter shall comply with all parts of this chapter. 
(Ord. of 4-7-2015) 
Secs. 6-152—6-170. - Reserved. 
Chapters 7—9 - RESERVED 
Chapter 10 - ANIMALS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Environment, ch. 26; disposal of dead animals, § 58-34. 
State Law reference— Authority to exercise animal control, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(3). 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 10-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Abandoned animal means any animal which shall have been placed upon public property or within a public building unattended or uncared for or upon or within the private property of another without the express permission of the owner, custodian or tenant of such private property and unattended or uncared for. An animal shall also be considered abandoned if the animal shall have been upon or within the property of the owner or custodian of the animal and unattended or without proper food and water for a period in excess of 36 hours. 
Animal at large means an animal not under restraint. 
Animal control center means the facility designated by the city manager for the detention of animals. 
Animal control superintendent means that person designated by the city manager to perform the duties prescribed by this chapter. 
Animal under restraint means any animal: 
(1)  Secured by a leash or lead or enclosed by a fence or other enclosure; 
(2)  Under the control of a responsible and competent person and obedient to that person's commands—that person being actually present with the animal; or 
(3)  Confined within a parked vehicle or a vehicle in motion. 
Companion animal means a domesticated animal kept as a pet for pleasure, rather than utility. Pets include but are not limited to birds, cats, dogs, hamsters, horses, mice, reptiles, domesticated wild animals, exotic animals and other animals associated with man's environment. 
Domesticated animal means any animal which is accustomed to living in or about the habitation of humans, including but not limited to cats, cows, dogs, fowl, horses, swine, domesticated wild animals and/or exotic animals. 
Guard dog means any dog which has been trained to attack persons or other animals independently or upon oral command or any dog which, while not so trained, is reasonably expected to perform as a guardian of the property upon and within which it is located. 
Owner means any person owning, possessing, keeping, harboring or acting as custodian of a domesticated animal. 
Vicious animal means: 
(1)  Any animal with a propensity, tendency or disposition to: 
a.  Attack; 
b.  Cause injury to; or 
c.  Otherwise endanger the safety of humans or other domestic animals. 
(2)  Any animal which attacks a human being or other domestic animal one or more times without provocation; or 
(3)  Any pit bull terrier, which is defined as any Staffordshire bull terrier breed of dog or any mixed breed of dog which contains an element of the breed of Staffordshire bull terrier or American Staffordshire terrier as to be identifiable as partially of the breed of Staffordshire bull terrier or American Staffordshire terrier by a qualified veterinarian duly licensed as such by the state. 
(Code 1977, § 4-22) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 10-2. - Purpose. 
The purpose of this chapter is to promote the health, safety, convenience, order, prosperity and welfare of the city's inhabitants. This chapter sets forth necessary controls on the unrestrained activities of animals which threaten the safety and pleasantness of streets, parks, sidewalks, yards and all areas of the city; and the lack of knowledge or intent is not a defense in the violation of this chapter. 
(Code 1977, § 4-21) 
Sec. 10-3. - Public nuisance. 
(a)  Any animal is declared to be a public nuisance if the animal: 
(1)  Is found at large in violation of section 10-4, 10-5, or 10-6; 
(2)  Is vicious, as defined in section 10-1, and while on the property of its owner is not kept enclosed by a fence at least five feet in height, the sides of which are embedded into the ground no less than one foot and the gate of which is secured by a child-proof lock, and restrained by a leash or chain to prevent it from wandering out of the confined area or while, off the real property of its owner, is not muzzled and kept secured by a leash or chain held by a competent person; 
(3)  Produces, because of quality, manner or method in which the animal is domesticated or maintained, unsanitary conditions in the city; 
(4)  Attacks passersby or passing vehicles; 
(5)  Makes or causes frequent or long continued noise which disturbs the comfort or repose of any person in the vicinity; or 
(6)  Is inimical to the public health, welfare or safety according to rules and regulations promulgated by the county board of health. 
(b)  Any person who knowingly keeps, owns, harbors or acts as custodian of an animal constituting a nuisance shall be guilty of an unlawful act and shall be punishable as provided in this chapter. 
(Code 1977, § 4-23) 
State Law reference— Dangerous Dog Control Law, O.C.G.A. § 4-8-20 et seq. 
Sec. 10-4. - Running at large. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for the owner of any animal or anyone having an animal in his custody to allow it to run at large unattended on or about the city streets and highways or on the property of another person without permission of the owner of the property or of the person in possession of that property. 
(b)  Penalties for violation of subsection (a) of this section are as follows: 
(1)  First offense ..... $ 25.00 
(2)  Second offense ..... 50.00 
(3)  Third offense ..... 100.00 
(4)  Fourth offense ..... 200.00 
(Code 1977, §§ 4-24, 4-28(d)) 
Sec. 10-5. - Restraint on property. 
It shall be the duty of every owner of any animal or anyone having any animal in his possession or custody to ensure that the animal is enclosed by a fence or other enclosure or is restrained by a chain or leash or in some other physical manner or under control by a competent person so that it cannot wander off the real property limits of its owner, possessor or custodian, except as provided in this chapter, it being the intent of this chapter that all animals be prevented from leaving while unattended the real property limits of their owners, possessors or custodians. 
(Code 1977, § 4-25) 
Sec. 10-6. - Restraint while off property. 
It shall be the duty of the owner of any animal or anyone having an animal in his possession to keep the animal under control at all times while the animal is off the real property limits of the owner, possessor or custodian. For the purpose of this section, an animal is deemed under control when it is confined within a vehicle, parked or in motion; is secured by a leash or other device held by a competent person; or is properly confined within an enclosure with permission of the owner of the property where the enclosure is located. 
(Code 1977, § 4-26) 
Sec. 10-7. - Prohibited in city parks and buildings. 
Animals are prohibited in city parks and city buildings; provided, however, that: 
(1)  Every totally or partially blind person shall have the right to be accompanied by a guide dog, and every physically disabled person and every deaf person shall have the right to be accompanied by a service dog, especially trained for the purpose, in any city park or city building; provided, however, that such person shall be liable for any damage done to the premises or facilities by such dog. The guide dog or service dog must be identified as having been trained by a school for Seeing Eye, hearing, service or guide dogs. 
(2)  Every person engaged in the training of a guide dog or service dog for the purpose of accompanying a person as provided in subsection (1) of this section shall have the same right to be accompanied by such dog being trained as the totally or partially blind person, deaf person or physically disabled person has under subsection (1) of this section so long as such trainer is identified as an agent or employee of a school for Seeing Eye, hearing, service or guide dogs. 
(Code 1977, § 4-24.1) 
Cross reference— Buildings and construction, ch. 14; parks and recreation, ch. 42. 
State Law reference— Right of disabled persons to use dogs in certain places, O.C.G.A. § 30-4-2. 
Sec. 10-8. - Wild animal permit. 
(a)  No person shall have, keep or maintain any wild, exotic, dangerous or nondomestic animal or reptile without first applying to and receiving from the police department a permit. The charge for this permit shall be $10.00. No such permit shall be issued if a permit required by O.C.G.A. title 27, ch. 5 (O.C.G.A. § 27-5-1 et seq.) has not been obtained. 
(b)  The police department is invested with the authority to issue a permit to any person for the keeping or maintaining of any wild, exotic, dangerous or nondomestic animal or reptile when, in the opinion of the police chief, any such animal or reptile may be kept or maintained without menacing the safety of any person or property. However, the police department may require any such animal or reptile to be properly caged or secured or may make additional rules or regulations regarding the keeping or maintaining of any such animal or reptile and may revoke any permit for any violation of any of the sections of this chapter or of any of the rules and regulations of the police department or when, in the opinion of the police chief, the safety of any person or property is menaced by the keeping of any such animal or reptile. 
(Code 1977, §§ 4-38, 4-39) 
Sec. 10-9. - Bird sanctuary. 
(a)  The city is declared a bird sanctuary. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to kill, destroy, harm or molest wild birds or fowl or their nests or eggs, except when a nuisance or threat to the public health exists, and then only as authorized by the city council. 
(Code 1977, § 4-1) 
Sec. 10-10. - Legal number of dogs and cats. 
It shall be unlawful and a public nuisance for any person in charge of a residence to keep or allow to be kept more than four dogs or four cats, or any combination of such animals exceeding four in number, over the age of 120 days at such residence unless the residence of all of the dogs and cats kept there are within a licensed kennel. 
(Ord. of 5-9-2006, § 10-2.6) 
Secs. 10-11—10-35. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Administration, ch. 2. 

Sec. 10-36. - Animal control center. 
The city council shall designate an area to be known as the city animal control center. 
(Code 1977, § 4-29(a)) 
Sec. 10-37. - Animal control superintendent. 
(a)  The city manager shall appoint a person to be known as animal control superintendent to supervise such other persons necessary to operate the animal control center. 
(b)  The animal control superintendent shall be charged with responsibilities, including but not limited to the following: 
(1)  Cooperating with the rabies control officer and county board of health and assisting in the enforcement of state laws with regard to dogs and especially with regard to the vaccination of such dogs against rabies and the confinement or leashing of vicious dogs; 
(2)  Investigating all complaints regarding animals; 
(3)  Issuing warning citations to offenders of this chapter; 
(4)  Enforcing, only through duly authorized personnel, all state laws, this Code and city ordinances for the care, control and custody of animals; 
(5)  Exacting, collecting, reporting and remitting fees and costs; and 
(6)  Supervising and being in charge of the city animal control center. 
(Code 1977, § 4-29(b), (c)) 
Cross reference— Administration, ch. 2. 
Sec. 10-38. - Violations. 
Upon information made known to the chief of police that any owner of any animal is in violation of this chapter, he shall cause a summons to be issued requiring such owner of such animal to appear before the judge of the municipal court on a day and time certain, then and there to stand trial for violation of this chapter. If a violation of this chapter has been personally witnessed to the chief of police, a subpoena shall be issued to the person making the complaint to appear on the day and time set for trial, then and there to testify on behalf of the city. 
(Code 1977, § 4-28(a)) 
Sec. 10-39. - Impoundment, redemption and destruction of animals. 
(a)  Except as stated in this section, any animal within the city without an owner, any animal running at large at any time or any animal within the city whose owner fails to have the animal vaccinated by a rabies inspector or licensed veterinarian, in accordance with state laws, shall be impounded or confined in the animal control center for a period of 120 hours. Any animal not redeemed in accordance with this section shall be destroyed in a humane manner. 
(b)  To the extent practicable, an animal running at large unattended and whose owner is known shall be taken to the owner's residence. If no adult person shall be present, it shall be taken to the animal control center. In either event, a redemption fee shall be paid by the owner in an amount of $25.00. 
(c)  If the owner of any animal is not known and such animal is upon the public streets, alleys, sidewalks, school grounds or other public places or premises or upon the property of another without the property owner's permission as prohibited by this chapter, upon complaint made to or information made known to the animal control department, it shall be the duty of the animal control superintendent to take possession of the animal and impound it in the animal control center as provided in this section. 
(d)  No later than two days after any animal has been taken to the animal control center, notice shall be given to its owner or, if the owner is unknown, notice shall be posted for five days, or until the animal is disposed of, on a bulletin board at city hall with a description of the animal and the time and place of taking the animal, together with the time and date of posting the notice. The time for the redemption of the animal as provided in this section shall not begin to run until such notice has been given or posted. 
(e)  In order for an owner to redeem an animal, the owner must have the animal fully vaccinated for rabies by an authorized rabies inspector or licensed veterinarian, if it has not been so vaccinated within one year from the redemption date, and shall pay a penalty in the amount of $10.00, plus the applicable fees as follows: 
(1)  Receiving at the pound ..... $10.00 
(2)  Housing, per day ..... 5.00 
(3)  Redemption ..... 25.00 
(f)  Any proceeds thus derived by the animal control center shall be turned over to the city clerk. 
(Code 1977, §§ 4-28(b), (c), 4-30, 4-31) 
Secs. 10-40—10-65. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - DOGS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 10-66. - Vaccinations for rabies. 
All dogs within the incorporated city limits shall be inoculated by a licensed veterinarian for the prevention of rabies. 
(Code 1977, § 4-27) 
Sec. 10-67. - Guard dogs. 
It shall be the duty of each owner, tenant or custodian of property upon or within which a guard dog is located to conspicuously and prominently post the following notice on the outside of the property: 
Warning  Guard Dog 
The notice shall be in either red or black letters upon a white background, large enough to be easily read at a distance of 25 feet. If the dog is in a building, the notice shall be conspicuously posted on or about each and every entrance and exit. If the guard dog is located in a general enclosure, the notices shall be conspicuously posted upon the enclosure at a distance not greater than 50 feet apart as well as upon each and every entrance and exit through the enclosure. If the guard dog is solely located within an apartment, a condominium or a building within a larger building, the notice shall be conspicuously posted on or about each and every entrance and exit. Failure to comply with this section shall be unlawful and shall be punishable as provided in this chapter. 
(Code 1977, § 4-32) 
Sec. 10-68. - Impoundment of rabies suspect or diseased dogs. 
Any dog impounded which appears to be suffering from rabies or is affected with hydrophobia shall not be redeemed but shall be kept for ten days under observation. Thereafter if the animal control officer determines that the dog is affected with the disease, the dog shall be destroyed in a humane manner. Otherwise it shall be subject to redemption as provided in this chapter. Any dog which is suffering from any infectious, contagious or dangerous disease may be redeemed by the owner in order to provide proper treatment for the dog. 
(Code 1977, § 4-33) 
Sec. 10-69. - Confinement for symptoms of rabies or for biting. 
(a)  Any dog which shows symptoms of rabies or which has bitten anyone shall be penned up immediately by its custodian, and the animal control center shall be notified immediately. The dog shall be confined in a place approved by the animal control superintendent and under conditions approved by him for not less than ten days, and the dog shall be subject to observation at all times during this period by a person designated by the animal control superintendent. 
(b)  If rabies does not develop within this period, the dog shall be released to its owner. If rabies does develop, the dog shall be destroyed in a humane manner. 
(Code 1977, § 4-34) 
Secs. 10-70—10-75. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - VICIOUS DOGS 

Sec. 10-76. - Requirements for possessing vicious dog or potentially vicious dogs. 
(a)  It is unlawful for an owner to have or possess within this state and the City of Lyons a vicious dog or potentially vicious dog without a certificate of registration issued in accordance with the provisions of this Code section. This certificate shall be in addition to any standard dog license and fees or other requirements of this chapter. 
(b)  Subject to the additional requirements of subsection (c) of this Code section for vicious dogs, the dog control officer shall issue a certificate of registration to the owner of such dog if the owner presents to the dog control officer or the dog control officer other wise finds sufficient evidence of: 
(1)  A proper enclosure to confine the vicious dog or potentially vicious dog, section 10-3. 
(2)  The posting of the premises where the vicious dog or potentially vicious dog is located with a clearly visible sign warning that there is a vicious dog on the property. This sign shall be designed by the department of natural resources and shall be posted in a conspicuous place so that it may be seen by the general public. 
(c)  In addition to the requirements of subsection (b) of this section, the owner of a vicious dog shall present to the dog control officer evidence of: 
(1)  A policy of insurance in the amount of at least $50,000.00 issued by an insurer authorized to transact business in this state insuring the owner of the vicious dog against liability for any personal injuries inflicted by the vicious dog; or 
(2)  A surety bond in the amount of $50,000.00 or more issued by a surety company authorized to transact business in this state payable to any person or persons injured by the dangerous dog. 
(d)  The owner of a vicious dog or potentially vicious dog shall notify the dog control officer within eight hours if the dog is on the loose, is unconfined, has attacked a human, has dies or has been sold or donated. If the dog has been sold or donated, the owner shall also provide the dog control officer with the name, address and telephone number of the new owner of the dog. 
(e)  The owner of a vicious dog or potentially vicious dog shall notify the dog control officer if the owner is moving from the City of Lyons. The owner of a vicious dog or potentially vicious dog who moves from this city to another jurisdiction with the state of Georgia shall register the vicious dog or potentially vicious dog in the new jurisdiction within ten days after becoming a resident. 
(f)  Issuance of a certificate of registration or renewal of a certificate of registration by the city does not warrant or guarantee that the requirements specified in subsections (b) or (c) of this section are maintained by the owner of a vicious dog or potentially vicious dog on a continuous basis following the date of issuance of the initial certificate of registration or following the date of any annual renewal of such certificate. 
(g)  A dog control officer is authorized to make whatever inquiry is deemed necessary to ensure compliance with the provisions of this chapter. 
(h)  The City of Lyons does hereby levy and charge against the owner of any vicious dog for the purpose of registration pursuant to this section, and in addition to any other license fees required generally for dogs within the city, the sum of $25.00 as a fee to register the dog as a vicious dog pursuant to the ordinances of the city. All certificates of registration shall be renewed on and annual basis. Annual renewal shall be at such time as all other business license is due (January 1—March 31). At the time of any renewal, the animal control officer shall require evidence from the owner or make such investigation as may be necessary from the owner or make such investigation as may be necessary to verify that the vicious dog, or potentially vicious dog, is continuing to be confined in a proper enclosure and that the owner is continuing to comply with all of the provisions of this Code which might apply to this situation. 
(Ord. of 5-9-2006, § 10-2.1) 
Sec. 10-77. - Restrictions on permitting vicious or potentially vicious dogs to be outside proper enclosure. 
(a)  It is unlawful for an owner of a vicious dog to permit the dog to be outside a proper enclosure unless the dog is muzzled and restrained by a substantial chain or leash and is under the physical restraint of a responsible person. The muzzle shall be made in a manner that will not cause injury to the dog or interfere with its vision or respiration but will prevent it from biting any person. 
(b)  It is unlawful for the owner of a potentially vicious dog to permit the dog to be outside a proper enclosure unless the dog is restrained by a substantial chain or leash and is under the restraint of a responsible person. 
(Ord. of 5-9-2006, § 10-2.2) 
Sec. 10-78. - Confiscation of dogs; grounds; disposition. 
(a)  A vicious dog shall be immediately confiscated by the dog control officer or by a law enforcement officer or by another person authorized by the city: 
(1)  Owner of the dog does not secure the liability insurance or bond required by subsection 10-76(c); 
(2)  Dog is not validly registered by section subsection 10-76(a); 
(3)  Dog is not maintained in a proper enclosure; or 
(4)  Dog is outside a proper enclosure in violation of subsection 10-3(a)(2) 
(b)  A potentially vicious dog shall be confiscated in the same manner as a vicious dog if the dog violates any part of section 10-3. 
(c)  Any dog that has been confiscated under the provisions of subsection (a) or (b) of this Code section shall be returned to its owner upon the owner's compliance with the provisions of this article and upon the payment of reasonable confiscation costs. In the event the owner has not complied with the provisions of this article within 120 hours the animal control officer will follow guidelines set forth in section 10-39. (Impoundment, redemption and destruction of animals) 
(Ord. of 5-9-2006, § 10-2.3) 
Sec. 10-79. - Violations; penalties. 
(a)  The owner of a vicious dog who violates the applicable provisions of sections 10-76 or 10-77 or whose vicious dog is subject to confiscation under subsection 10-78(a), be guilty of a misdemeanor of high and aggravated nature. In addition to any confinement that might be imposed for a conviction under this subsection, for a second conviction a fine of not less than $500.00 shall be imposed and for a third or subsequent conviction a fine of not less than $750.00 shall be imposed. 
(b)  The owner of a potentially vicious dog who violates the applicable provisions of sections 10-76 or 10-77 or whose potentially vicious dog is subject to confiscation under subsection 10-78(a), shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. In addition to any confinement that might be imposed for a conviction under this subsection, for a second conviction a fine of not less than $150.00 shall be imposed and for a third or subsequent conviction a fine of not less than $300.00 shall be imposed. 
(c)  If an owner who has a previous conviction for a violation of this article knowingly and willfully fails to comply with the provisions of this division, such owner shall be guilty of a felony if the owner's vicious dog attacks or bites a human being under circumstances constituting another violation of this division. The owner of a vicious dog who is convicted for a violation of this subsection shall be punished by a fine of not less than $1,000.00 nor more than $5,000.00 or by imprisonment for not less than one nor more than five years or by both such fine and imprisonment. 
(d)  In addition to the penalties for violations under subsection (c) or (d) herein, the vicious dog involved shall be immediately confiscated by the dog control officer or by a law enforcement officer or another person authorized by the city and placed in quarantine for the proper length of time as determined by the county board of health, and, thereafter, the vicious dog shall be destroyed in and expeditious and humane manner. 
(e)  No owner of a vicious dog shall be held criminally liable under this division for injuries inflicted by said owner's dog to any human being while on the owner's properties. 
(Ord. of 5-9-2006, § 10-2.4) 
Sec. 10-80. - Liability for damages. 
It is the intent of the State of Georgia and the City of Lyons that the owner of a vicious dog or potentially vicious dog shall be solely liable for injury to or death of a person caused by such a dog. Under no circumstances shall the city or any employee or official which enforces or fails to enforce the provisions of this division be held liable for any damages to any person who suffers and injury inflicted by a dog or by a dog that has been identified as being a vicious or potentially vicious dog or by a dog that has been reported to the proper authorities as being a vicious or potentially vicious dog or by a dog that the city has failed to identify as a vicious dog or potentially vicious dog but has not been kept or restrained in the manner described in subsection 10-3(2) or by a vicious dog or potentially vicious dog whose owner has not maintained insurance coverage or a surety bond as required by subsection 10-76(c). Enacted by GA. L. 1989, p. 159, section 5). 
(Ord. of 5-9-2006, § 10-2.5) 
Secs. 10-81—10-95. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - LIVESTOCK 

Sec. 10-96. - Keeping, maintaining, raising or feeding. 
It shall be unlawful to keep, maintain, raise or feed any livestock within the city, except as authorized in this article. 
(Code 1977, § 4-2) 
Sec. 10-97. - Maximum period for keeping or maintaining. 
Except as authorized in this article, it shall be unlawful to maintain or keep or cause to be maintained or kept within the city any livestock for any purpose whatsoever for a period longer than 48 hours, including the keeping or maintaining of any such animals for the purpose of sale or shipping. 
(Code 1977, § 4-3) 
Sec. 10-98. - Animal hospital conditions. 
(a)  Livestock, while under medical treatment at an animal hospital operated by a licensed veterinarian, may be kept within the city only when: 
(1)  Screened in; 
(2)  Proper fly extermination measures are practiced; 
(3)  The city sewer system is not stopped up or damaged in carrying off the waste products of such animals; and 
(4)  The premises are maintained in a sanitary manner. 
(b)  Any animal hospital shall use a flow of water in cleaning the premises sufficient to prevent stopping and clogging up the city sewer system. In addition to punishment of the offending party as provided in section 1-7, the city shall assess the offending party with the full expense to the city, including labor and materials, caused by stoppage of the sewer system due to waste products of any animals. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful to maintain any animal hospital in the city without having first obtained a certificate or written statement from the state health department that proper sanitary standards are maintained. 
(Code 1977, §§ 4-4—4-6) 
Secs. 10-99—10-125. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - CRUELTY AND RELATED OFFENSES[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference— Cruelty to animals, O.C.G.A. § 16-12-4; Georgia Animal Protection Act, O.C.G.A. § 4-11-1 et seq. 

Sec. 10-126. - Teasing, molesting and poisoning. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to tease, molest, bait, poison or in any way bother any animal not belonging to him or legally under his control. 
(Code 1977, § 4-35) 
Sec. 10-127. - Notice of injury to companion animals. 
It shall be unlawful for any person injuring a companion animal by running over it or into the animal or coming into contact with it with an automobile, motorcycle, bicycle or other vehicle to fail to immediately notify the owner of the animal, the animal control center or the police department. 
(Code 1977, § 4-36) 
Sec. 10-128. - Abandonment. 
It shall be unlawful for anyone to knowingly abandon any animal within the city. Each person who does abandon knowingly or who willingly permits such abandonment or who aids in the abandonment of any animal shall be in violation of the law. 
(Code 1977, § 4-37) 
Chapters 11—13 - RESERVED 
Chapter 14 - BUILDINGS AND CONSTRUCTION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted July 14, 2015, amended ch. 14 in its entirety, in effect repealing and reenacting said chapter to read as set out herein. The former ch. 14, §§ 14-1—14-5 and § 14-31 pertained to similar subject matter and derived from §§ 5-2—5-5, 5-40, and §§ 21-51—21-54 of the 1977 Code and a resolution adopted Nov. 2, 2004. 
Cross reference— Animals prohibited in city parks and buildings, § 10-7; blighted property, § 26-56 et seq.; derelict property, § 26-90 et seq.; environment, ch. 26; fire prevention and protection, ch. 30; fire prevention code, § 30-2; flood damage prevention, ch. 32; natural resources, ch. 34; planning, ch. 50; signs, ch. 54; solid waste, ch. 58; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 62; subdivisions, ch. 66; utilities, ch. 74; zoning, app. A. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 14-1. - Fire district. 
The city fire district shall comprise the central business district as defined and delineated in the zoning ordinance in appendix A to this Code. 
(Ord. of 7-14-2015(1)) 
Sec. 14-2. - Permit fees. 
The fees to be charged for any permit issued under the provisions of this article shall be as established by the mayor and council from time to time and on file in the office of the city clerk. 
(Ord. of 7-14-2015(1); Ord. of 5-2-2017) 
Sec. 14-3. - Water conservation requirements for certain plumbing fixtures. 
(a)  The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Commercial means any type of building other than residential. 
Construction means the erection of a new building or the alteration of an existing building in connection with its repair or renovation or in connection with making an addition to an existing building and includes the replacement of a malfunctioning, unserviceable, or obsolete faucet, showerhead, toilet or urinal in an existing building. 
Residential means any building or unit of a building intended for occupancy as a dwelling, but does not include a hotel or motel. 
(b)  There shall not be initiated within this city the construction of any residential building of any type which: 
(1)  Employs a gravity tank-type, flushometer-valve or flushometer-tank toilet that uses more than an average of 1.6 gallons of water per flush; 
(2)  Employs a showerhead that allows a flow of more than an average of 2.5 gallons of water per minute at 60 pounds per square inch of pressure; 
(3)  Employs a urinal that uses more than an average of 1.0 gallon of water per flush; 
(4)  Employs a lavatory faucet or lavatory replacement aerator that allows a flow of more than 2.0 gallons of water per minute; or 
(5)  Employs a kitchen faucet or kitchen replacement aerator that allows a flow of more than 2.5 gallons of water per minute. 
(c)  There shall not be initiated within this city the construction of any commercial building of any type which does not meet the requirements of subsections (b)(1) through (5) of this section. 
(d)  The requirements of subsection (b) of this section shall apply to any residential construction initiated after April 1, 1992, and to any commercial construction initiated after July 1, 1992, which involves the repair or renovation of or addition to any existing building when such repair or renovation of or addition to such existing building includes the replacement of toilets or showers or both. 
(e)  The requirements of subsections (b), (c) and (d) of this section, relative to new construction and to the repair or renovation of an existing building, shall apply under the following conditions: 
(1)  When the repair or renovation of the existing building does not include the replacement of the plumbing or sewer system servicing toilets, faucets or showerheads within such existing building; 
(2)  When such plumbing or sewer system within such existing building, because of its capacity, design or installation, would not function properly if the toilets, faucets or showerheads required by this section were installed; 
(3)  When such system is a well or gravity flow from a spring and is owned privately by an individual for use in such individual's personal residence; or 
(4)  When units to be installed are: 
a.  Specifically designed for use by persons with disabilities; 
b.  Specifically designed to withstand unusual abuse or installation in a penal institution; or 
c.  Toilets for juveniles. 
(f)  The owner or his agent of a building undergoing new construction or repair or renovation who is entitled to an exemption as specified in subsection (e)(2), (3) or (4) of this section shall obtain the exemption by applying at the office of the building inspector. A fee of $25.00 shall be charged for the inspection and issuance of such exemption. 
(g)  This section shall not apply to any construction of a residential building, the contract for which was entered into prior to April 1, 1992, and shall not apply to any construction of a commercial building, the contract for which was entered into prior to July 1, 1992. 
(h)  Any person who installs any toilet, faucet, urinal, or showerhead in violation of this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(i)  The sale of a gravity tank-type, flushometer-valve or flushometer-tank toilet that uses more than an average of 1.6 gallons of water per flush shall be prohibited. 
(j)  This section shall be enforced by the building inspector. Citations for violations may be issued by the chief building inspector. 
(Ord. of 7-14-2015(1)) 
Sec. 14-4. - Display of house or building numbers. 
House or buildings numbers shall be clearly displayed on all houses or buildings, and failure to do so shall be a violation of this Code section, punishable by a $10.00 fine. 
(Ord. of 7-14-2015(1)) 
Secs. 14-5—14-40. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - CONSTRUCTION STANDARDS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 14-41. - State minimum standard codes. 
(a)  Codes which are to be enforced by city manager or his designated representatives. The minimum standard codes enumerated in O.C.G.A. § 8-2-20(9)(B)(i)(I)—(VIII), to-wit: 
(1)  International Building Code (ICC); 
(2)  National Electrical Code (NFPA); 
(3)  International Fuel Gas Code (ICC); 
(4)  International Mechanical Code (ICC); 
(5)  International Plumbing Code (ICC); 
(6)  International Residential Code for One- and Two-Family Dwellings (ICC); 
(7)  International Energy Conservation Code (ICC); and 
(8)  International Fire Code (ICC); 
Which codes have mandatory statewide application and do not require adoption by local ordinance, shall be enforced by the city manager, his designated representative, or designee(s) thereof, in accordance with the procedures hereinafter set forth. 
(b)  Adoption of optional codes; enumeration. There is hereby adopted within the city the optional state minimum standard codes enumerated in O.C.G.A. § 8-2-20(9)(B)(i)(IX)—(X), to-wit: 
(1)  International Existing Building Code (ICC); and 
(2)  International Property Maintenance Code (ICC); 
(c)  The codes provided in subparts (a) and (b) of this section shall mean the current edition of such codes as approved by board of community affairs, within the state department of community affairs, including any new edition of any such code as provided in O.C.G.A. § 8-2-23; and provided, further, that any such codes may hereafter be amended or revised as provided in O.C.G.A. § 8-2-23 and all amendments or appendices of such codes are hereby adopted and deemed included or incorporated herein. All references to "State Minimum Standard Codes" shall include the Georgia State Amendments promulgated by the board of community affairs and any local amendments approved by said board. 
(d)  Whenever the International Fire Code (ICC), as approved by the board of community affairs, is applicable, any state minimum standard code provision shall not be less restrictive than the Georgia State Fire Code, as adopted by the state safety fire commissioner pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 25-2-13. 
(e)  The city manager or his designee shall make copies of relevant sections of the codes enforced or adopted in this section available to members of the general public, in printed or written format, at such price as it deems reasonable, to defray the costs of publication and handling. Due to copyright limitations, copying or duplication of some codes may be restricted. 
(Ord. of 7-14-2015(1)) 
Sec. 14-42. - Duties and responsibilities of city manager or his designated representatives. 
(a)  Primary administration and enforcement of construction codes is vested in the city manager, who may appoint one or more building inspectors and delegate such functions as the manager, in his discretion, deems appropriate. Where more than one building inspector is employed, the manager may designate a chief building inspector to administratively head the department of building and code enforcement. The manager, and his designated representatives, shall have and exercise the following duties and responsibilities in the enforcement of state minimum standard codes: 
(1)  To interpret, enforce, and administer the state minimum standard codes within the city in accordance with the provisions and procedural requirements of this article; 
(2)  To inspect all existing buildings and structures as required by such codes and to permit and inspect new construction and the renovation, alteration, modification and repairs to existing structures to assure compliance with applicable state minimum code standards; 
(3)  Under the budget and personnel regulations of said city, to employ inspectors and other personnel necessary for the proper enforcement of such codes and to provide for the authority, functions, and duties of such inspectors; 
(4)  To bring enforcement actions, prosecute complaints and citations in the appropriate court and to appeal those decisions adverse to the best interest of the city; 
(5)  To study and make recommendations to the city council on ordinances relating to the administration and enforcement of state minimum standard codes; and 
(6)  To perform all other duties and functions imposed upon the chief administrative officer, by whatever name or title referred, in the state minimum standard codes. 
(b)  The duties and responsibilities of the manager and his designated representatives, set forth in this section, may, by private or intergovernmental contract approved by the city council, be exercised and performed by an independent contractor or by the city manager or his designated representative of any county or other municipal corporation of this state. When such contract has been entered and spread upon the official minutes of the commission, the acts of such contractor shall be deemed the acts of the city as if fully performed directly by the city, its officers and employees. 
(Ord. of 7-14-2015(1)) 
Sec. 14-43. - Limitation of liability for code enforcement; no special duty created. 
It is the intent of this article to protect the public health, life safety and general welfare of properties and occupiers of buildings and structures within the city in general, but not to create any special duty or relationship with any individual person or to any specified property within or without the boundaries of the city. Approval of a permit and inspection of a property shall in no manner guarantee or warrant to the owner or occupants thereof that said property has been constructed, maintained, or operated in conformance with applicable codes, laws and regulations. The city reserves the right to assert all available immunities and defenses in any action seeking to impose monetary damages upon the city, its officers, employees and agents arising out of any alleged failure or breach of duty or relationship as may now exist or hereafter be created. To the extent any federal or state law, regulation, or ordinance requires compliance as a condition precedent to the issuance of a permit, plan or design approval, inspection or other activity by the city, its officers, employees and agents, issuance of such permit, approval, or inspection shall not be deemed to constitute a waiver or estoppel of the condition precedent, and it shall remain the obligation and responsibility of the owner, his design professional(s), and contractor(s) to satisfy such legal requirements. 
(Ord. of 7-14-2015(1)) 
Secs. 14-44—14-65. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PERMIT PROCEDURES AND ENFORCEMENT 

Sec. 14-66. - Permits. 
(a)  Required. No person, firm, corporation, company or other entity, or any agent of such person, firm, corporation, company or other entity, shall erect, construct, enlarge, alter, repair, move, improve, convert or demolish any building or structure within the city, or cause the same to be done, without first obtaining a permit for such building or structure from the city, except as may otherwise be allowed by this chapter. Separate permits are required for grading, electrical, plumbing and/or gas. 
(b)  Fees. Permit fees shall be set forth in a schedule approved by the city council, pursuant to ordinance or resolution, and may be revised from time to time. 
(c)  Term. Permits shall generally be good for six months from date of issuance; provided, that if the work is not completed within the initial permit term, but has been diligently pursued, the permit may be extended, without additional charge, for successive three-month terms, so long as the work continues to be diligently prosecuted. 
(d)  Revocation for suspension or abandonment. If work authorized by a permit is suspended or abandoned, after the initial term, for a period of 30 days, without good cause shown to the city manager or his designated representative, the permit may be revoked upon written notification to the permit holder. Revocations of permits for abandonment are not appealable to the city council. 
(e)  State licensing required. Persons engaging in construction, electrical, plumbing, gas, mechanical, low-voltage or utility contracting on any work within the city are required to possess a license issued by the state construction licensing industry board as a condition for performing the work; provided, however, the owner of a single-family dwelling performing work (other than utility contracting) within a dwelling occupied by him as his personal residence, shall be exempt from state licensing. Where a state license is required, every applicant for a permit shall furnish proof, at time of application, that he or the person contracted to do the work holds a valid state license in good standing. Failure to meet this requirement may be grounds for revocation of the permit. 
(Ord. of 7-14-2015(1)) 
Sec. 14-67. - Written documentation; payment of fee required for issuance. 
Prior to issuance of any permit, in addition to the information requested on the permit application, the city manager or his designated representative may require tests, plans and specifications, plats, and other written documentation from engineers, architects, surveyors, and other professionals to assure that full compliance with all permitting requirements of the state minimum standard codes and applicable laws have been met. No permits shall issue on any project where the structure to be built or improved thereon is a "special hazard structure" or the use to be conducted therein is a "special hazard use", without first obtaining the approval of building plans by the state fire marshal's office. Where a project is subject to permitting under the state soil erosion and sedimentation control law, no permit shall issue for any land-disturbance activity unless approved plans are received from the district soil conservation office and all required stabilization facilities are in place, and ready for inspection. All buildings and structures intended for human occupancy shall have a safe source of drinking water and sanitary disposal; no permit shall issue for any building or structure which does not have access to public water and sewer unless plans for a well and/or septic tank have been approved by the county health department. All permits shall be conditioned upon the application and supporting data, which is deemed incorporated into and made a material part or term of the permission granted. No permit shall issue until all requisite fees have been paid in full. 
(Ord. of 7-14-2015(1)) 
Sec. 14-68. - Cessation of work. 
Upon notice from the city manager or his designated representative, work on any building, structure, system or component therein, that is being done contrary to the provisions of the state minimum standard codes, or in a dangerous or unsafe manner, or in violation of any other applicable law, rule, or regulation, shall immediately cease. Such notice shall be given in writing, directed to the owner of the property and to the person doing the work, and shall state the conditions under which work may be resumed. Where an emergency situation exists, the city manager or his designated representative shall not be required to give a written notice prior to stopping the work. 
(Ord. of 7-14-2015(1)) 
Sec. 14-69. - Revocation of permit for false statement or misrepresentation. 
The city manager or his designated representative may revoke a permit or approval issued under the provisions of this article in the event he finds there has been a false statement or misrepresentation as to any material fact in the application or plans on which the permit or approval was based. The city manager or his designated representative may also revoke a permit upon determining that the construction, erection, alteration, repair, moving, or demolition of the building or structure for which the permit was issued is in violation of, or not in conformity with, the provisions of state minimum standard codes; provided, the work was stopped in accordance with section 14-68 and the permittee has not met the conditions for resuming the work after a reasonable period for compliance has been granted. 
(Ord. of 7-14-2015(1)) 
Sec. 14-70. - Inspections; right of entry.
