(2)  Conservation or preservation of soil, water, vegetation, fish, or other wildlife, provided they do not affect waters of the State of Georgia or of the United States in such a way that would require a Section 404 permit; 
(3)  Outdoor passive recreational activities, including fishing, hunting, bird watching, hiking, biking, boating, horseback riding, kayaking, and canoeing; 
(4)  Natural water quality treatment or purification; and 
(5)  Normal agriculture activities, including the planting and harvesting of crops and pasturing of livestock (such activities shall be subject to best management practices approved by the Georgia Department of Agriculture). 
(Ord. No. 1308, § 1, 4-3-2018) 
Sec. 34-105. - Prohibited uses. 
In compliance with the Georgia "Rules for Environmental Planning Criteria," the following uses are prohibited entirely and no permit shall be issued for them: 
(1)  Receiving areas for toxic or hazardous waste or other contaminants; and 
(2)  Hazardous or sanitary waste landfills. 
(Ord. No. 1308, § 1, 4-3-2018) 
Secs. 34-106—34-135. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - GROUNDWATER RECHARGE AREAS PROTECTION REGULATIONS 

Sec. 34-136. - Findings of fact. 
Recharge areas are vulnerable to urban development activities as well as agricultural activities. Pesticides and herbicides sprayed on crops and animal waste, like septic tank affluents, contribute to a deterioration in the groundwater quality and can threaten the health of residents of the city relying on well water. Development usually means an increase in the amount of land covered with impervious surfaces. Paving land in recharge areas can alter or impair their recharge characteristics thereby decreasing groundwater supplies. 
(Ord. No. 1308, § 1, 4-3-2018) 
Sec. 34-137. - Reference map. 
The official map for delineation of significant groundwater recharge areas in the city to be regulated areas under this article is the Georgia Department of Natural Resources' "Significant Recharge Areas, Hydrological Atlas 18 (1989 edition)." 
(Ord. No. 1308, § 1, 4-3-2018) 
Sec. 34-138. - Groundwater recharge areas development permit requirements. 
All uses, except those identified in section 34-139 and those subject to further restrictions by any underlying zoning district, are allowed. The following are additional requirements for specific uses: 
(1)  All new above ground chemical or petroleum storage tanks, having a minimum volume of 660 gallons, shall have secondary containment for 110 percent of the volume of such tanks or 110 percent of the volume of the largest tank in a cluster of tanks, and shall otherwise meet the requirements of US EPA rules for oil pollution prevention, 40 CFR 112.1, et. seq. Such tanks used for agricultural purposes are exempt, provided they comply with all federal and state requirements; 
(2)  All single-family dwellings, multi-family dwellings, mobile home parks, or other uses, which are located within a groundwater recharge area and not served by both public water and sewer systems, shall be required to have 150 percent of the minimum lot or space size calculated based on application of the Georgia Department of Public Health Manual for On-Site Sewage Management Systems (DPH Manual) Tables MT-1 and MT-2 (included as part of this article in Appendix I), as determined by the county health department. The minimums set forth in Tables MT-1 and MT-2 may be increased further based on consideration of other factors (set forth in Sections A-F) of the public health manual. Said minimum lot size shall not be in any case less than the minimum lot size specified by any underlying zoning district. The regulations or determination specifying the largest minimum lot size shall apply; 
(3)  All lots shall have a minimum width of 150 feet, or as specified in any underlying zoning district if stricter (larger), in the area where an approved on-site sewage management system is to be located; 
(4)  No construction may proceed on a building or mobile home to be served by a septic tank or other on-site sewage management system unless the county health department first approves the proposed on-site sewage management system installation as meeting the requirements of the Georgia Department of Public Health Manual for on-site sewage management systems and the applicable provisions of this article; 
(5)  All new wastewater treatment basins shall have an impermeable liner except for the construction of mining settling basins; and 
(6)  All new agricultural waste impoundment sites shall be lined. As a minimum, the liner shall be constructed of compact clay having a thickness of one-foot and a vertical hydraulic conductivity of less than 5 x 10" 7 cm/sec or other criteria established by the U.S. Natural Resources Conservation Service, or the Environmental Protection Division. 
(Ord. No. 1308, § 1, 4-3-2018) 
Sec. 34-139. - Prohibited uses. 
The following uses are prohibited entirely and no permit shall be issued for them: 
(1)  All new hazardous waste storage, treatment and disposal facilities; 
(2)  New facilities handling hazardous materials regulated by the Georgia Department of Natural Resources as to require a permit; 
(3)  Permanent storm water infiltration basins; and 
(4)  All new sanitary or other landfills. 
(Ord. No. 1308, § 1, 4-3-2018) 
Secs. 34-140—34-170. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - MAJOR RIVER CORRIDOR PROTECTION DISTRICT REGULATIONS 

Sec. 34-171. - Findings of fact. 
Perennial river or water courses with an average annual flow of at least 400 cubic feet per second are of vital importance to the State of Georgia in that they help preserve those qualities that make a river suitable for habitat for wildlife, a site for recreation, and a source for clean drinking water. These river corridors also allow the free movement of wildlife from area to area within the state, help control erosion and river sedimentation, and help absorb flood waters. 
(Ord. No. 1308, § 1, 4-3-2018) 
Sec. 34-172. - District delineation. 
Protected rivers as defined under the Rules for Environmental Planning Criteria, adopted by the Georgia Department of Natural Resources pursuant to O.C.G.A § 12-2-8, includes any perennial river or water courses with an average annual flow of at least 400 cubic feet per second. The Altamaha River and the Ohoopee River through Toombs County and meet this criteria. A protected river corridor and a protective 100 foot natural vegetative buffer, as defined in Georgia Department of Natural Resources Environmental Protection Division's Rules for Environmental Planning Criteria Chapter 391-3-16, is hereby established along the entire length of this river(s) within the jurisdiction of Toombs County. The buffer area is measured horizontally from each river bank, if any, within the city. Under the method prescribed by the Rules for Environmental Planning Criteria, no development or other land disturbing activity will be allowed to occur within the protected river corridor and within a 100 foot buffer of the river bank except for certain permitted uses as set forth in section 34-173. 
(Ord. No. 1308, § 1, 4-3-2018) 
Sec. 34-173. - Permitted uses. 
No development, or construction, or other land disturbing activity shall occur within the 100 foot buffer from the protected river except for the following permitted uses, as long as they do not impair the long term functions of the protected river or the protected river corridor. In addition, the natural vegetative buffer shall be restored as quickly as possible following any land-disturbing activity or construction within the river corridor in connection with the following permitted uses: 
(1)  Single-family dwellings, if any underlying zoning district so permits, provided each dwelling is located on a lot with a minimum size as specified by the county health department or the underlying zoning district regulations, but shall be the greater of these requirements; however, in any case the lot for each dwelling shall not be less than two acres, not including any area between the river banks; and provided the septic tank drain field is located outside of the 100 foot buffer area; 
(2)  Any residential use existing or under construction prior to the date of the adoption of this article; provided that, such use has an on-site sewage management construction permit issued by the county health department prior to the date of adoption of this article; 
(3)  Any industrial or commercial use existing prior to the date of the adoption of this article; provided that, such use does not impair the drinking quality of the river water as defined by the federal Clean Water Act, as amended, and meets all other federal and state environmental rules and regulations; 
(4)  Road and utility crossings, and utility locations if no other location is reasonable, providing the construction of these crossings and uses meet the requirements of the Georgia Erosion and Sedimentation Act of 1975, as amended, or any other state or local requirements, if stricter, protect the integrity of the buffer area to the extent reasonably possible, and are located as far from the river bank as is reasonably possible; 
(5)  Timber production and harvesting; provided that, it is consistent with the best management practices established by the Georgia Forestry Commission, and does not impair the drinking quality of the river water as defined by the federal Clean Water Act, as amended; 
(6)  Agricultural production and management; provided that, it is consistent with the best management practices established by the Georgia Soil and Water Conservation Commission or its successor, and all other state and federal laws and regulations, including those promulgated by the Georgia Department of Agriculture; and does not impair the drinking quality of the river water as defined by the federal Clean Water Act, as amended; 
(7)  Wildlife and fisheries management activities consistent with the purposes of O.C.G.A. § 12-2-8, as amended; 
(8)  Natural water quality treatment or purification; 
(9)  Wastewater treatment; and 
(10)  Recreational usage consistent with the maintenance of a natural vegetative buffer or with river dependent recreation. 
(Ord. No. 1308, § 1, 4-3-2018) 
Sec. 34-174. - Prohibited uses. 
In compliance with the Georgia "Rules for Environmental Planning Criteria," the following uses are prohibited entirely and no permit shall be issued for them: 
(1)  Facilities or areas used for the handling, receiving, storing, or disposal of hazardous wastes; 
(2)  Hazardous or solid waste landfills; 
(3)  Septic tank drain fields within the 100-foot buffer area under any circumstance; and 
(4)  Septic tanks within the 100-foot buffer area, except as expressly provided for single-family dwellings which are permitted under section 34-173. 
(Ord. No. 1308, § 1, 4-3-2018) 
Secs. 34-175—34-200. - Reserved.

Chapters 35—37 - RESERVED 
Chapter 38 - OFFENSES AND MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Traffic and vehicles, ch. 70. 
State Law reference— Criminal Code of Georgia, O.C.G.A. § 16-1-1 et seq.; authority to adopt ordinances for the purpose of preserving public health, safety and welfare, O.C.G.A. § 36-1-20(a). 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 38-1. - Drinking in public. 
No person shall drink any alcoholic beverage in streets, alleys, parks, motor vehicles, or any public place or place where the public is invited, except such places as are licensed to pour alcoholic beverages. 
(Code 1977, § 14-10) 
Cross reference— Alcoholic beverages, ch. 6. 
Sec. 38-2. - Possession of marijuana. 
Any person convicted in the municipal court of possession of less than one ounce of marijuana shall be fined $150.00 and/or confined in jail for 60 days. 
(Code 1977, § 14-6) 
State Law reference— Drug offenses, O.C.G.A. § 16-13-2 et seq.; jurisdiction of municipal court over marijuana cases, O.C.G.A. § 36-32-6. 
Secs. 38-3—38-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - OFFENSES INVOLVING PUBLIC SAFETY 

Sec. 38-31. - Turkey shoots. 
Turkey shoots are prohibited within the city. 
(Code 1977, § 14-3) 
Sec. 38-32. - Loitering. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to be found within any public or private building, after being requested by the owner or person in charge thereof to leave. 
(Code 1977, § 14-5) 
Secs. 38-33—38-60. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - OFFENSES INVOLVING PUBLIC PEACE AND ORDER 

Sec. 38-61. - Disorderly conduct. 
(a)  Scope of violation. Any person who shall use loud, boisterous or obscene language or who shall fight, quarrel or make any unnecessary noise or do any other thing or act within the corporate city limits calculated to disturb the peace, quiet and good order of the city or of any person within the city limits shall be guilty of the offense of disorderly conduct. 
(b)  Defense to charge. It shall be a full defense to any charge under this section that the offense charged was committed in the reasonable defense of person, family, habitation or property against unprovoked or unlawful attack, assault or trespass; but for a mutual consent to fight, both persons shall be guilty of the offense. 
(c)  Fine for disorderly fighting. The fine for disorderly fighting is $200.00 for the first offense. 
(Code 1977, § 14-9) 
Sec. 38-62. - Congregating to obstruct streets. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to occupy the streets or sidewalks or for a number of persons to congregate in such numbers on the city sidewalks or streets so as to obstruct the sidewalks or streets. 
(Code 1977, § 14-2) 
Cross reference— Streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 62. 
State Law reference— Obstructing highways, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-43; unlawful assembly, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-33. 
Sec. 38-63. - Hunting inside city limits. 
No hunting or discharging of firearms shall be allowed within the city limits. 
(Code 1977, § 14-11) 
Sec. 38-64. - Indecent exposure. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to appear in any public place or in view of the public wearing pants or shorts below the waist, which exposes the skin or undergarments. 
(b)  Any person violating the provision of this section shall upon conviction thereof be fined not less than $50.00 and not more than $250.00 and be ordered to perform not less than 20 hours or more than 80 hours of community service. 
(Mo. of 8-2-2011) 
Secs. 38-65—38-80. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - OFFENSES INVOLVING PUBLIC HEALTH 

Sec. 38-81. - Use of tobacco products on city property prohibited. 
(a)  Unlawful use of tobacco products. It shall be unlawful for any person to use any form of tobacco, including, but not limited to cigarettes, E-cigarettes, cigars, tobacco pipes, chewing tobacco, and any form of smokeless tobacco at, in or on any indoor or outdoor facilities owned or operated by the City of Lyons, including, but not limited to all public buildings, city-owned vehicles and equipment, real property, parking lots, restrooms, parks, athletic fields, and walking/hiking trails leased, owned or maintained by the city. 
(b)  Signage. The city shall cause appropriate signs to be posted sufficient to inform the public and all city employees of the prohibition on the use of tobacco products as set forth in subsection (a). 
(c)  Enforcement. City staff[,] city police and code enforcement officers shall make periodic inspection of all city property and facilities to monitor for compliance with this section of the Code. 
(1)  Employees of the city that knowingly use tobacco products in violation of this section shall be subject to disciplinary action. Repeated violations of this section by employees of the city may result in disciplinary action, including, but not limited to written reprimand, suspension from employment without pay, or dismissal for cause. 
(2)  Any other person(s) found in violation of the prohibition on the use of tobacco products set forth in this section shall be entitled to one verbal warning by a city police or code enforcement officer a staff member of the city prior to enforcement of this section by issuance of a citation by a law enforcement officer[,] city police or code enforcement officer. 
(3)  The minimum fine for the first conviction of violating this section within 12 months shall be $50.00. Subsequent violations within the same 12-month period by the same individual shall double for each violation up to a maximum of $800.00. 
(4)  The city recommends the Georgia Tobacco Quit Line (1-800-270-7867), a toll free resource operated by the Georgia Cancer Coalition, for those members of the public and employees of the city that are attempting to quit tobacco use. More information is available at www.georgiacancer.org/prev-quitline.php. 
(Ord. of 3-4-2014) 
Chapters 39—41 - RESERVED 
Chapter 42 - PARKS AND RECREATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Animals prohibited in city parks and buildings, § 10-7; environment, ch. 26; natural resources, ch. 34; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 62. 
State Law reference— Authority to construct and operate parks, swimming pools, golf courses, recreation grounds and buildings used for sports, O.C.G.A. § 36-34-3; authority to provide parks, recreation areas, programs and facilities, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(5). 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 42-1—42-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PUBLIC CONDUCT IN PARKS 

Sec. 42-26. - Curfew. 
There shall be a curfew on all city parks from 11:00 p.m. until daybreak. Any unauthorized person found therein during such hours shall be fined $35.00. 
(Code 1977, § 14-7) 
Sec. 42-27. - Young children accompanied by older person. 
Children under six years of age must be accompanied by a person 13 years of age or older while in all city parks. 
(Code 1977, § 14-8) 
Sec. 42-28. - Alcoholic beverages. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to consume or possess any alcoholic beverages, liquors, wines or other intoxicating spirits in any park owned or maintained by or on behalf of the city. 
(b)  Any person seeking admittance to the parks shall submit to a search of his person and vehicle by any officer of the police department in order to prevent the transportation of any alcoholic beverages, liquors, wines, or other intoxicating spirits into the parks. Any person refusing to allow his person or vehicle to be searched shall be refused admittance to the parks. 
(c)  Any person convicted of violating this section shall be fined up to $100.00 and/or confined in jail for seven days and not allowed to use the park facilities for a period not to exceed six months. 
(Code 1977, § 14-8.1) 
Cross reference— Alcoholic beverages, ch. 6. 
Secs. 42-29—42-40. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - RECREATION BOARD[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted April 1, 1994 set out provisions intended for use as Art. III, §§ 42-30—42-40. To preserve the style of this Code, and at the editor's discretion, these provisions have been included as §§42-41—42-51. 

Sec. 42-41. - Creation; purpose. 
The mayor and city council hereby determine that the power to provide, establish, conduct, and maintain a recreation system for the city shall be vested in and exercised by a recreation board, hereafter called "recreation board", and the same is hereby established. 
(Ord. of 4-1-1994) 
Sec. 42-42. - Membership. 
The recreation board shall consist of six members. 
(Ord. of 4-1-1994) 
Sec. 42-43. - Appointment; terms of members. 
The term of office of the members of the recreation board shall be for three years and until their successors are appointed and qualified, except that for and at the pleasure of the mayor and city council, any member of said board may be dismissed from office and a new member appointed to fill his unexpired term, and except that the terms of such board members shall be that two members' terms shall expire each year hereafter. Members whose terms expire in any given year shall be eligible for reappointment. The membership of the board shall annually submit to the mayor and council the name or names of prospective members for appointment. The mayor and council reserve the power to approve or reject such nominations and fill vacancies of unexpired terms. 
(Ord. of 4-1-1994) 
Sec. 42-44. - Organization. 
The recreation board shall meet at least once a month. Immediately after January 1 or each year, the members shall meet and organize by electing one of their members as chairman and such other officers as may be necessary. 
(Ord. of 4-1-1994) 
Sec. 42-45. - Adoption of bylaws, rules and regulations. 
The recreation board shall have power to adopt bylaws, rules and regulations for the conduct of its affairs and for the proper conduct of recreation in the city. 
(Ord. of 4-1-1994) 
Sec. 42-46. - Control; regulation of activities and facilities. 
The recreation board shall provide, conduct and supervise public playgrounds, playfields, indoor recreation centers and other recreation facilities now owned or controlled by the city. It shall have power to conduct any form of recreation or cultural activity that will employ the leisure time of the people, in a wholesome or constructive manner. It may conduct such activities on properties under its own control, on public properties with the consent of the authorities thereof, and on private properties with the consent of the owners. 
(Ord. of 4-1-1994) 
Sec. 42-47. - Appointment of director of recreation; other personnel. 
The recreation board shall have the power to appoint and designate a person to act as director of recreation, who is trained and properly qualified for the work, and the power to appoint such other personnel as the recreation board deems proper, subject to approval by the mayor and city council. 
(Ord. of 4-1-1994) 
Sec. 42-48. - Submission; approval of budget. 
Annually the recreation board shall submit a budget to the mayor and council for its approval. 
(Ord. of 4-1-1994) 
Sec. 42-49. - Soliciting; receiving gifts and bequests. 
The recreation board may solicit or receive gifts or bequests of money or other personal or real property or any donation to be applied either principal or income or both, for either temporary or permanent use for playgrounds or other recreational purposes. 
(Ord. of 4-1-1994) 
Sec. 42-50. - Reports required. 
The recreation board or the director of recreation shall make an annual report to the mayor and council, and shall make such other reports as from time to time may be requested of it by the mayor and council. 
(Ord. of 4-1-1994) 
Sec. 42-51. - Application; effect of state law. 
This article is adopted under the provisions of the Act of Legislature approved February 1, 1946 appearing in Georgia Law 1946, page 152 et seq., and the recreation board herein created shall have all powers and duties provided in that act. 
(Ord. of 4-1-1994)

Editor's note— Ord. No. 1263, § 2, adopted December 4, 2017, repealed ch. 46, §§ 46-1—46-4, 46-31—46-36 and appendix A and enacted a new ch. 46 as set out herein. Former ch. 46 pertained to similar subject matter and derived from the Code of 1977.

State Law reference— Power to define, regulate and alter the powers, duties, qualifications, compensation and tenure of municipal officers, agents and employees, O.C.G.A. § 36-34-2(2). 

ARTICLE I. - CITY RETIREMENT SYSTEM 

Sec. 46-1. - Establishment of plan to provide retirement and benefits for employees. 
O.C.G.A. § 47-5-40 provides that, by ordinance, the governing authority of the city is empowered to establish a plan or plans for the provision of retirement or employee benefits for its employees and that the ordinance shall set forth the employees to be covered, the benefits to be provided, and the conditions of the plan. Pursuant to a duly approved ordinance on August 5, 2014, the city has restated, confirmed and enacted the retirement plan for the employees of the city in accordance with and subject to the terms and conditions set forth in the adoption agreement, any addendum to the adoption agreement, the Georgia Municipal Employees Benefit System (GMEBS) Master Plan Document, and the GMEBS Trust Agreement, and the foregoing documents and instruments have been approved by authorized officers of the city and GMEBS, such that the foregoing shall constitute a contract between the city and GMEBS, all as authorized and provided by O.C.G.A. § 47-5-1 et seq. 
(Ord. No. 1263, § 2, 12-4-2017) 
Sec. 46-2. - Fixing of rights and obligations of former employees and officers. 
Except as otherwise specifically required by law or by the terms of the master plan or adoption agreement (or any addendum), the rights and obligations under the plan with respect to persons whose employment with the city was terminated or who vacated his or her office with the city for any reason whatsoever prior to the effective date of this ordinance are fixed and shall be governed by such plan, if any, as it existed and was in effect at the time of such termination. 
(Ord. No. 1263, § 2, 12-4-2017) 
Secs. 46-3—46-30. - Reserved.

Chapter 50 - PLANNING[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Administration, ch. 2; buildings and construction, ch. 14; environment, ch. 26; natural resources, ch. 34; signs, ch. 54; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 62; subdivisions, ch. 66; utilities, ch. 74; zoning, app. A.

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 50-1. - Altamaha-Georgia Southern Area Planning and Development Commission. 
There is hereby adopted the ordinance to establish the Altamaha-Georgia Southern Area Planning and Development Commission, which ordinance is on file in the city clerk's office. 
(Code 1977, § 17-5) 
Secs. 50-2—50-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PLANNING COMMISSION[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Cross reference— Boards, commissions and authorities, § 2-101 et seq. 

Sec. 50-31. - Created. 
The city planning commission hereby created. 
(Code 1977, § 17-1) 
Sec. 50-32. - Membership. 
(a)  The planning commission shall consist of five members, who shall be city residents, appointed by the city council. 
(b)  The terms of the members shall be for four years. Any vacancy in membership shall be filled for the unexpired term by the city council, who shall also have the authority to remove any member for cause, on written charges, after a public hearing. 
(c)  All members shall serve without compensation, but may be reimbursed for actual expenses incurred in connection with their official duties. 
(Code 1977, § 17-2) 
Sec. 50-33. - Organization; rules; staff; finances. 
(a)  The planning commission shall elect its chairman from among its members. The term of the chairman shall be one year, with eligibility for reelection. 
(b)  The planning commission shall appoint a secretary, who may be a city officer or employee. 
(c)  The planning commission shall make its own rules of procedure and determine its time of meeting. All meetings of the planning commission at which official action is taken shall be a public record. 
(d)  The planning commission may appoint such employees and staff as it may deem necessary for its work and may contract with the state planning agency and city planners and other consultants for such services as it may require. 
(e)  The expenditures of the planning commission, exclusive of gifts, shall be within the amounts appropriated for the purpose by the city council. 
(Code 1977, § 17-3) 
Sec. 50-34. - Powers and duties. 
From and after the time the planning commission shall have organized and selected its officers and shall have adopted its rules of procedure, such planning commission shall have all the powers, duties and responsibilities set forth in 1957 Ga. Laws (Act No. 358). 
(Code 1977, § 17-4)

Chapter 54 - SIGNS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Buildings and construction, ch. 14; planning, ch. 50; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 62; zoning, app. A. 
State Law reference— Signs used by retail distilled spirits dealers, signs advertising Georgia lottery, O.C.G.A. § 3-4-3; control of signs and signals, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-50 et seq.; unlawful placement of signs within right-of-way of public road, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-51; outdoor advertising near state highways, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-70 et seq. 

Sec. 54-1. - Outdoor advertising signs. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to erect, place or maintain any outdoor advertising sign which: 
(1)  Outdoor advertising signs may be erected in the commercial and industrial districts of the city. All structures will be composed of metal and steel construction. The maximum area of any outdoor advertising sign shall not exceed 300 square feet in sign area. Such area not to include as part of the measurement the structural components or trim of such sign. No outdoor advertising sign shall be erected to exceed 30 feet above grade of highway. If additional height is needed a conditional use permit may be issued. No outdoor advertising sign shall exceed 50 feet in length and the bottom coping of sign shall be a minimum of three feet above ground level. 
(2)  Contains more than one face visible from the same direction on the main traveled way. Back-to-back, and V-type constructed signs shall, for the purpose of determining compliance with size and spacing limitation, be considered as one sign. 
(3)  Is within 500 feet of a public park, public playground, public recreation area, public forest scenic area, cemetery, church or historic landmark. 
(4)  All outdoor advertising signs permitted to be erected under this chapter shall not be erected after the passage of this chapter unless the sign to be erected is spaced a minimum of 1,500 feet from a then existing outdoor advertising sign on either side of the road as measured along a parallel to such road. This spacing does not include back-to-back, or V-type sign structures, as such sign structures are considered one sign structure for spacing requirements. Side-by-side signs are not allowed. No signs shall be stacked one above the other. No sign shall be erected or maintained within 20 feet of the nearest edge of any right-of-way or public utility easement. This distance shall be measured from the nearest outer edge of the sign. 
(5)  All illuminated outdoor advertising signs shall be so illuminated so as to adhere to the customary practices of the industry in the state at the time of passage of this chapter, providing that no light device shall be used which in any way initiates any traffic control device, railroad sign or signal, or highway directional sign, or law enforcement of emergency vehicle lights, or in any manner flashing lights to a residential zone, or in any way creates a traffic hazard. 
(6)  No outdoor advertising sign shall be erected or maintained which is in an area not zoned for commercial or industrial activity and within 300 feet in any direction from a residence without the written consent of such residential property owner. 
(7)  No person shall engage within the corporate limits of the city in the business of erecting or maintaining outdoor advertising signs as required under this chapter until after such persons shall have filed with the city clerk evidence of liability insurance coverage of $50,000.00 property damage, $100,000.00 personal injury to any one person and $200,000.00 for personal injury growing out of any one occurrence. Such liability insurance will save and keep the city, and all of its officials, employees and agents, harmless from all damages, liabilities, losses or judgments resulting by reason of the erection or maintenance of any such sign, and of any injury to persons or damages to property resulting therefrom. 
(Code 1977, § 17.5-21; Ord. of 1-5-1999) 
Chapters 55—57 - RESERVED 
Chapter 58 - SOLID WASTE[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Buildings and construction, ch. 14; environment, ch. 26; natural resources, ch. 34; utilities, ch. 74. 
State Law reference— Georgia Comprehensive Solid Waste Management Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-20 et seq.; Georgia Hazardous Waste Management Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-60 et seq.; Litter Control Law, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-40 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 58-1. - Multijurisdictional solid waste management resolution adopted. 
The resolution regarding the county multijurisdictional solid waste management plan, performed under the county board of commissioners, is hereby adopted by reference. At least one copy thereof is on file in the office of the city clerk. 
(Code 1977, § 18-1) 
State Law reference— Local, multijurisdictional and regional solid waste plans, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-31.1. 
Secs. 58-2—58-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL 

Sec. 58-31. - Dumping at landfill by residents only. 
There shall be no dumping at the city sanitary landfill other than by city residents. 
(Code 1977, § 18-2) 
Sec. 58-32. - Garbage pickup fees. 
The garbage pickup fees shall be as prescribed from time to time by the city council. 
(Code 1977, § 18-3) 
Sec. 58-33. - Placement of trash receptacles by businesses. 
Receptacles for trash shall be placed at the back entrance of business houses. 
(Code 1977, § 18-4) 
Sec. 58-34. - Disposal of dead animals. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to bury, dispose of, or burn any carcass of any dead animal, such as dogs, hogs, cows, mules, or of other description, within the city upon any private property, street, alley, lane, lot or other property except at the city sanitary landfill, unless such burning is personally supervised by the chief of police or a member of the police department. 
(b)  Any animal described in subsection (a) of this section that is taken, hauled or carried to the city sanitary landfill shall be buried not less than four feet deep in the ground, and the grave or hole in which such animal is buried must be covered level with the ground with earth, sand or cement. The sanitary landfill shall be the only place in which any dead animal may be taken, carried or dumped. 
(Code 1977, § 18-5) 
Cross reference— Animals, ch. 10. 
State Law reference— Dead Animal Disposal Act, O.C.G.A. § 4-5-1 et seq. 
Sec. 58-35. - Fee for debris removal from city right-of-ways. 
Effective January 1, 2005, a fee of $1.50 per month will be assessed every household and business within the city. The purpose of this fee is to help defray the cost of maintaining the city's rights-of-way and the inert landfill in a neat, orderly and sanitary manner. The fee will be included in the monthly water bill as designated as a tipping fee. 
(Res. of 12-7-2004) 
Editor's note— A resolution of Dec. 7, 2004, added provisions to the Code, but did not specify manner of inclusion. Therefore, at the discretion of the editor, said provisions have been included herein as § 58-35. 
Cross reference— Utilities, ch. 74. 
Chapters 59—61 - RESERVED 
Chapter 62 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND OTHER PUBLIC PLACES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Any ordinance dedicating, establishing, naming, locating, relocating, opening, paving, widening, repairing or vacating any street, sidewalk or alley saved from repeal, § 1-12(11); buildings and construction, ch. 14; cemeteries, ch. 22; environment, ch. 26; flood damage prevention, ch. 32; natural resources, ch. 34; congregating to obstruct streets, § 38-62; parks and recreation, ch. 42; planning, ch. 50; signs, ch. 54; subdivisions, ch. 66; traffic and vehicles, ch. 70; riding bicycles on sidewalks, § 70-4; towing of vehicles parked in alleys, § 70-32; one-way streets and alleys, § 70-65; utilities, ch. 74; vehicles for hire, ch. 78; zoning, app. A. 
State Law reference— State, county and municipal road systems, O.C.G.A. § 32-4-1 et seq.; powers with respect to municipal street system, O.C.G.A. § 32-4-92; municipal street improvements, O.C.G.A. § 36-39-1 et seq.; authority to construct and maintain roads, including curbs, sidewalks, street lights and devices to control the flow of traffic, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(4). 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 62-1. - Placing obstructions on streets and sidewalks. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to place any mobile sign, wrecker, lumber, merchandise or other obstruction on any streets or sidewalks in the city. 
(Code 1977, § 19-1) 
State Law reference— Obstructing sidewalks or other public passages, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-43. 
Sec. 62-2. - Street openings. 
No street shall be opened which has not been deeded to the city prior to beginning any work. 
(Code 1977, § 19-2) 
Secs. 62-3—62-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PARADES[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Parades and processions generally, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-7, 40-6-76; authority to regulate parades and processions preserved, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-371(a)(3). 

DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 62-31. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Parade means any parade, march, demonstration, ceremony, show, exhibition, pageant, or procession of any kind, or any similar display, in or upon any street or other public place. 
(Code 1977, § 14-1) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 62-32. - Exemptions. 
This article shall not apply to the following: 
(1)  Funeral processions. 
(2)  Students going to and from school classes or participating in educational activities, providing such conduct is under the immediate direction and supervision of the proper school authorities. 
(3)  A governmental agency acting within the scope of its functions. 
(Code 1977, § 14-1) 
Secs. 62-33—62-60. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PERMIT 

Sec. 62-61. - Required. 
No person shall engage in, participate in, aid, form or start any parade, without a parade permit issued by the city clerk. 
(Code 1977, § 14-1) 
Sec. 62-62. - Application. 
(a)  A person desiring a parade permit shall file an application with the city clerk on forms provided by such officer. Such application shall be filed not less than seven days nor more than 60 days before the date on which it is proposed to conduct the parade. 
(b)  The application for a parade permit shall set forth the following information: 
(1)  The name, address and telephone number of the person seeking to conduct such parade. 
(2)  If the parade is proposed to be conducted for, on behalf of or by an organization, the name, address and telephone number of the headquarters of the organization and the names, addresses and telephone numbers of the authorized and responsible heads of such organization. 
(3)  The name, address and telephone number of the person who will be the parade chairman and who will be responsible for its conduct. 
(4)  The date when the parade is to be conducted. 
(5)  The route to be traveled, the starting point and the termination point. 
(6)  The approximate number of persons who and animals and vehicles which will constitute such parade, the type of animals, and description of the vehicles. 
(7)  The hours when such parade will start and terminate. 
(8)  A statement as to whether the parade will occupy all or only a portion of the width of the streets proposed to be traversed. 
(9)  The location by streets of any assembly areas for such parade. 
(10)  The time at which units of the parade will begin to assemble at any such assembly area. 
(11)  The interval of space to be maintained between units of the parade. 
(12)  If the parade is designed to be held by and on behalf of or for any person other than the applicant, a communication in writing from the person proposing to hold the parade, authorizing the applicant to apply for the permit on his behalf. 
(13)  Any additional information which the city clerk shall find reasonably necessary to a fair determination as to whether a permit should be issued. 
(c)  The city clerk, where good cause is shown therefor, shall have the authority to consider any such application which is filed less than seven days before the date the parade is proposed to be conducted. 
(Code 1977, § 14-1) 
Sec. 62-63. - Issuance standards. 
The city clerk shall issue a parade permit when, from a consideration of the application and from such other information as may otherwise be obtained, he finds that: 
(1)  The conduct of the parade will not substantially interrupt the safe and orderly movement of other traffic contiguous to its route. 
(2)  The conduct of the parade will not require the diversion of so great a number of police officers to properly police the line of movement and the areas contiguous thereto as to prevent normal police protection. 
(3)  The conduct of such parade will not require the diversion of so great a number of ambulances as to prevent normal ambulance service to portions of the city other than that to be occupied by the proposed line of march and areas contiguous thereto. 
(4)  The concentration of persons, animals and vehicles at assembly points of the parade will not unduly interfere with proper fire and police protection of or ambulance service to areas contiguous to such assembly areas. 
(5)  The conduct of such parade will not interfere with the movement of firefighting equipment en route to fire. 
(6)  The conduct of the parade is not reasonably likely to: 
a.  Cause injury to persons or property; 
b.  Provoke disorderly conduct; or 
c.  Create a disturbance. 
(7)  The parade is scheduled to move from its point of origin to its point of termination expeditiously and without unreasonable delays en route. 
(8)  The parade is not to be held for the sole purpose of advertising any product, cause, goods or events and is not designed to be held purely for private profit. 
(Code 1977, § 14-1) 
Sec. 62-64. - Notice of denial. 
If the city clerk disapproves the application for a parade permit, he shall mail to the applicant, within three days after the date upon which the application was filed, a notice of his action. 
(Code 1977, § 14-1) 
Sec. 62-65. - Alternate permit. 
The city clerk, in denying an application for a parade permit, shall be empowered to authorize the conduct of the parade on a date, at a time, or over a route different from that named by the applicant. An applicant desiring to accept an alternate permit shall, within five days after notice of the action of the city clerk, file a written notice of acceptance with the city clerk. An alternate parade permit shall conform to the requirements of and shall have the effect of a parade permit under this division. 
(Code 1977, § 14-1) 
Sec. 62-66. - Contents. 
Each parade permit shall state the following information: 
(1)  Starting time. 
(2)  Minimum speed. 
(3)  Maximum speed. 
(4)  Maximum interval of space to be maintained between the units of the parade. 
(5)  The portions of the streets to be traversed that may be occupied by the parade. 
(6)  The maximum length of the parade in miles. 
(7)  Such other information as the city clerk shall find necessary to the enforcement of this article. 
(Code 1977, § 14-1) 
Sec. 62-67. - Revocation. 
The city clerk shall have the authority, after a hearing affording due process, to revoke a parade permit upon application of the standards for issuance as set forth in this division. 
(Code 1977, § 14-1) 
Sec. 62-68. - Compliance with laws and regulations. 
A person holding a parade permit shall comply with all permit directions and conditions and with all applicable laws and ordinances. 
(Code 1977, § 14-1)

(Mo. of 11-4-1969) 
Chapter 67 - RESERVED 
Chapter 68 - TAXATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted Dec. 7, 2004, set out provisions intended for use as Ch. 20, §§ 20-31—20-41. To conform to the alphabetical arrangement of chapters, and at the editor's discretion, these provisions have been included as Ch 68, §§ 68-31—68-41. 
Cross reference— Administration, ch. 2; businesses, ch. 18. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 68-1—68-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - LODGING TAX[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Lodging tax, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-50. 

Sec. 68-31. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms, and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning. 
Due date. From the 20th day after the close of the monthly period for which tax is to be computed. 
Guest room. A room occupied, or intended, arranged, or designed for occupancy, by one or more occupants for the purpose of living quarters or residential use. 
Hold. Any structure or any portion of a structure, including any lodging house, rooming house, dormitory, Turkish bath, bachelor hotel, studio hotel, motel, motor hotel, auto court, inn, public club, or private club, containing guest rooms and which is occupied, or is intended or designed for occupancy, by guests, whether rent is paid in money, goods, labor, or otherwise. "Hotel" does not include any jail, hospital, asylum, sanitarium, orphanage, prison, place of detention, or other buildings in which human beings are housed and detained under legal restraint. 
Monthly period. The calendar months of any year. 
Occupancy. The use or possession, or the right to use or possession of any room or apartment in a hotel or the right to the use or possession of the furnishings or to the services and accommodations accompanying the use and possession of the room. 
Occupant. Any person who, for a consideration, uses, possesses, or has the right to use or possess any room in a hotel under any lease, concession, permit, right of access, license to use or other agreement, or otherwise. 
Operator. Any person operation a hotel in the city, including, but not limited to, the owner or proprietor of such premises, lessee, sub-lessee, lender in possession, license or any other person otherwise operating such hotel. 
Permanent resident. Any occupant as of a given date who has or shall have occupied or has or shall have the right of occupancy of any guest room in a hotel for at least ten consecutive days next preceding such date. 
Person. An individual, firm, partnership, joint adventure, association, social club, fraternal organization, joint stock company, corporation, nonprofit corporation or co-operative nonprofit membership, estate, trust, business trust, receiver, trustee, syndicate, or any other group or combination acting as a unit, the plural as well as the singular number, excepting the United States of America, the state, and any political subdivision of either thereof upon which the city is without power to impose the tax herein provided. 
Rent. The consideration received for occupancy valued in money, whether received in money or otherwise, including all receipts, cash, credits, and property or services of any king or nature, and also the amount for which credit is allowed by the operator to the occupant, without any deduction there from whatsoever. 
Return. Any return filed or required to be filed as provided in this article. 
Tax. The tax imposed by this article. 
(Ord. of 12-7-2004, § 20-31) 
Sec. 68-32. - Imposition and rate of tax. 
There shall be paid a tax of five percent of the rent for every occupancy of a guest room in a hotel in the city. The tax imposed by this article shall be paid upon any occupancy on and after January 1, 2005, although such occupancy is had pursuant to a contract, lease or other arrangement made prior to such date. 
(Ord. of 12-7-2004, § 20-32) 
Sec. 68-33. - Exemptions. 
No tax shall be imposed under this article upon a permanent resident or upon state or local government officials or employees when traveling on official business. 
(Ord. of 12-7-2004, § 20-33) 
Sec. 68-34. - Collection of tax by operator; receipt to occupant; rules for collection schedules. 
(a)  Every operator maintaining a place of business in this city, as provided in section 68-31 and renting guest rooms in this city, not exempted under section 68-33 shall collect a tax of five percent on the amount of rent from the occupant. 
(b)  Such operator shall provide a receipt to each occupant to whom the tax is charged, showing the amount of rent and the amount of all taxes by category. 
(c)  All taxes due shall be collected at the same time as rent is collected. 
(Ord. of 12-7-2004, § 20-34) 
Sec. 68-35. - Registration of operator, form and contents; execution; certificate of authority. 
Every person engaging or about to engage in business as an operator of a hotel in this city shall register with the city clerk or the clerk's designee of the city, on a form provided by the city clerk or the clerk's designee. Such registration shall set forth the name under which such person transacts business or intends to transact business, the location of his/her place of business and such other information which would facilitate the collection of the tax as the city clerk or the clerk's designee may require. The registration shall be signed by the owner if a natural person; in case of ownership by as association or partnership, by a member or partner, in the case of ownership by a corporation, by an officer. The city clerk or the clerk's designee shall, after such registration, issue without a charge a certificate of authority to each operator to collect the tax from the occupant. A separate registration shall be required for each place of business of an operator. Each certificate shall state the name and location of the business to which it is applicable. 
(Ord. of 12-7-2004, § 20-35) 
Sec. 68-36. - Determination, returns and payments. 
(a)  Due date of taxes. All amount of such taxes shall be due and payable to the city clerk or the clerk's designee monthly on or before the 20th day of every month next succeeding each respective monthly period as set forth in section 68-31. 
(b)  Return; time of filing; persons required to file; contents. On or before the 20th day of the month following each monthly period, a return for the preceding monthly period shall be filed with the city clerk or the clerk's designee showing the gross rent, rent from permanent residents, taxable rent, amount of tax collected or otherwise due for the related period, and such other information as may be required by the city clerk or the clerk's designee. 
(c)  Collection fee allowed operators. Operators collecting the tax shall be allowed a percentage of the tax due and accounted for and shall be reimbursed in the form of a deduction in submitting, reporting and payment of the amount due, if said amount is not delinquent at the time of payment. The rate of the deduction shall be the same rate authorized for deductions from state tax under O.C.G.A. tit. 48, ch. 8, art. 1 (O.C.G.A. § 48-8-1 et seq.) as now or hereafter amended. 
(Ord. of 12-7-2004, § 20-36) 
Sec. 68-37. - Deficiency determinations. 
(a)  Recomputation of tax; authority to make; basis of recomputation. If the city clerk or the clerk's designee is not satisfied with the return or returns of the tax or the amount of the tax required to be paid to the city by any person, the clerk or clerk's designee may compute and determine the amount required to be paid upon the basis of any information within the possession of the clerk or clerk's designee or that may come into such person's possession. One or more deficiency determinations may be made of the amount due for one or more monthly period. 
(b)  Interest on deficiency. The amount of the determination shall bear interest at the rate of three-fourths of one percent per month, or fraction, thereof from the due date of taxes. 
(c)  Service of notice of determination. The city clerk or the clerk's designee or designated representative shall give to the operator written notice of such determination. The notice may be served personally or by mail; if by mail, such service shall be addressed to the operator at the operator's address as it appears in the records of the city clerk or the clerk's designee. Service by mail is complete when delivered by certified mail with a receipt signed by addressee. 
(d)  Time within which notice of deficiency determination to be mailed. Except in the case of failure to make a return, every notice of a deficiency determination shall be mailed within three years after the 20th day of the calendar month following the monthly period for which the amount is proposed to be determined, or within three years after the return is filed, whichever period should least expire. 
(Ord. of 12-7-2004, § 20-37) 
Sec. 68-38. - Determination if no return made. 
(a)  Estimate of gross receipts. If any person fails to make a return, the city clerk or the clerk's designee shall make an estimate of the amount of the gross receipts of the person, or as the case may be, of the amount of the total rentals in this city which are subject to the tax. The estimate shall be made for the period or periods in respect to which the person failed to make the return and shall be based upon any information which is or may come into the possession of the city clerk or the clerk's designee. Written notice shall be given in the manner prescribed in section 68-37. 
(b)  Interest on amount found due. The amount of the determination shall bear interest at rate of three-fourths of one percent per month, or fraction thereof, from the 20th day of the month following the monthly period, for which the amount or any portion thereof should have been returned, until the date of payment. 
(Ord. of 12-7-2004, § 20-38) 
Sec. 68-39. - Administration. 
(a)  Authority of city official. The city clerk or the clerk's designee shall administer and enforce the provisions of this article for the collection of the tax imposed by this article. 
(b)  Records required from operators, etc., form. Every operator renting guest rooms in this city to a person shall keep such records, receipts, invoices, and other permanent papers in such form as the city clerk or the clerk's designee may require. 
(c)  Examination of records; audits. The city clerk or the clerk's designee or any person authorized in writing by the city clerk or the clerk's designee may examine the books, papers, records, financial reports, equipment and other facilities of any operator renting guest rooms to a person and any operator liable for the tax, in order to verify the accuracy of any return made, or if no return is made by the operator, to ascertain and determine the amount required to be paid. 
(d)  Authority to require reports; contents. In administration of the provisions of this article, the city clerk or the clerk's designee may require the filing of reports by any person or class of persons having possession or custody of information relating to rentals of guest rooms which are subject to the tax. The reports shall be filed with the city clerk or the clerk's designee when required by the city clerk or the clerk's designee and shall set forth the rental charged for each occupancy, the date or dates of occupancy, and such other information as the city clerk or the clerk's designee may require. 
(Ord. of 12-7-2004, § 20-39) 
Sec. 68-40. - Collection of tax. 
(a)  Action for tax. At any time within three years after any tax or any amount of tax required to be collected becomes due and payable and at any time within three years after the delinquency of any tax or any amount of tax required to be collected, the city clerk or the clerk's may bring an action in a court of competent jurisdiction in the name of the city to collect the amount delinquent together with interest, court fees, filing fees, attorney's fees and other legal fees incident thereto. 
(b)  Duty of successors or assignees of operator to withhold tax from purchase money. If any operator liable for any amount under this article sells out such business or quits the business, the successors or assigns shall withhold sufficient of the purchase price to cover such amount until the former owner produces a receipt from the city clerk or the clerk's designee showing that payment has been made or a certificate stating that no amount is due. 
(c)  Liability for failure to withhold; certificate of notice of amount due; time to enforce successor's liability. If the purchaser of a business fails to withhold purchase price as required, such purchaser shall be personally liable for the payment of the amount required to be with held by such purchaser to the extent of the purchase price. 
(d)  Tax credit, or interest paid more than once or erroneously or illegally collected. Whenever the amount or any tax or interest has been paid more than once, or has been erroneously or illegally collected or received by the city under this article, it may be offset by the city clerk or the clerk's designee. If the operator or person determines that the operator or person has over paid or paid more than once, which fact has not been determined by the city clerk or the clerk's designee, the operator or person will have three years from date of payment to file claim in writing stating the specific ground upon which the claim is founded. The claim shall be audited. If the claim is approved by the city clerk or clerk's designee, the excess amount it was paid, or such person's administrator or executors. 
(Ord. of 12-7-2004, § 20-40) 
Sec. 68-41. - Violations. 
Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall be deemed guilty of an offense and upon conviction thereof shall be punished as provided in section 1-10 of this Code. Any operator or any other person who fails to register as required herein, or to furnish any data required by the city clerk or the clerk's designee or who renders a false or fraudulent return shall be deemed guilty of an offense and upon conviction thereof shall be punished as aforesaid. 
(Ord. of 12-7-2004, § 20-41) 
Sec. 68-42. - Tax expenditure. 
Taxes collected shall be disbursed as required by O.C.G.A. § 48-13-51(a)(4.6)(A). 
(Ord. of 8-2-2005) 
Chapter 69 - RESERVED 
Chapter 70 - TRAFFIC AND VEHICLES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Flood damage prevention, ch. 32; offenses and miscellaneous provisions, ch. 38; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 62; vehicles for hire, ch. 78. 
State Law reference— Traffic generally, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-1 et seq.; powers of local authorities, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-370 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 70-1. - Uniform rules of the road. 
The provisions of O.C.G.A. § 40-6-1 and definitions of O.C.G.A. § 40-1-1 are hereby incorporated herein by reference and adopted as and for the traffic regulations of this city with like effect as if recited in this chapter. Unless another penalty is expressly provided by law, every person convicted of a violation of this section shall be guilty of an offense. 
(Code 1977, §§ 20-1—20-3; Ord. No. 1322B, § I, 8-7-2018) 
State Law reference— Authority to so provide, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-372 et seq. 
Sec. 70-2. - Off-road vehicles. 
(a)  Definition. As used in this section, the term "off-road vehicle" means any motorized vehicle designed for or capable of cross-country travel on or immediately over land, water, snow, ice, marsh, swampland, or other natural terrain and not intended for use predominantly on public roads. It includes, but is not limited to, four-wheel drive or low-pressure-tire vehicles, two-wheeled vehicles, amphibious machines, ground-effect or air-cushion vehicles, and any other means of transportation deriving power from any source other than muscle or wind. However, such term shall exclude the following: 
(1)  Any motorboat; 
(2)  Any military, fire, or law enforcement vehicle; 
(3)  Any vehicles used exclusively on airports; 
(4)  All farm machinery, farm tractors, and other self-propelled equipment for harvesting and transportation of forest products, clearing of land for planting, utility, service and maintenance, and earth moving, construction, or mining; and 
(5)  Self-propelled lawn mowers, snow blowers, garden or lawn tractors, or golf carts, while such vehicles are being used exclusively for their designed purposes. 
(b)  Operating instructions. Any person operating an off-road vehicle under any of the following conditions shall be deemed to be in violation of this section and subject to the penalties provided in subsection (c) of this section: 
(1)  Without operative brakes or without mufflers or other silencing equipment; 
(2)  On any private property without the express written permission of the owner of the property or his agent; or 
(3)  On any city street, highway, or alley. 
(c)  Enforcement and penalties. All law enforcement officers shall enforce this section within the city. Any person who violates this section shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punished by a fine not to exceed $25.00. 
(Code 1977, § 20-12; Ord. No. 1322B, § I, 8-7-2018) 
State Law reference— Similar provisions, O.C.G.A. §§ 40-7-3, 40-7-6; authority to adopt rules consistent with state law for off-road vehicles, O.C.G.A. § 40-7-5. 
Sec. 70-3. - Riding bicycles on sidewalks. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to ride a bicycle on the sidewalk on any city street. 
(Code 1977, § 20-9; Ord. No. 1322B, § I, 8-7-2018) 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 1322B, § I, adopted August 7, 2018, repealed § 70-3 and renumbered § 70-4 as § 70-3. Former § 70-3 pertained to licensing of wreckers and derived from the Code of 1977 and an ordinance adopted August 7, 2007. 
Cross reference— Streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 62. 
State Law reference— Bicycles, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-290 et seq. 
Secs. 70-4—70-30. - Reserved.

ARTICLE IV. - LOW SPEED MOTOR VEHICLES 

Sec. 70-81. - Short title. 
This article shall be known as the "Lyons Low Speed Motor Vehicle Ordinance." 
(Ord. of 9-3-2013) 
Sec. 70-82. - Definitions. 
[The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:] 
All-terrain vehicle means any motorized vehicle designed for off-road use which is equipped with three or more low pressure tires and with a seat to be straddled by the operator and with handlebars for steering control. 
Drivers license means any license to operate a motor vehicle issued under the laws of the State of Georgia or any other state. 
Low speed motor vehicle (LSMV) means those electric and gasoline-powered pleasure carts, commonly called "golf carts" which when operated, are incapable of being operated at speeds in excess of 20 miles per hour and have at least three or more wheels. Low speed motor vehicle shall also mean any four-wheeled electric vehicle whose top speed attainable in one mile is greater than 20 miles per hour but not greater than 25 miles per hour on a paved level surface and which is manufactured in compliance with those federal motor vehicle safety standards for low-speed vehicles set forth in 49 CFR 571.500 and in effect January 1, 2001. 
Operator means any person who drives or is in actual physical control of a motor vehicle. 
Owner means a person, other than a lienholder or security interest holder, having the property in or title to a vehicle. The term includes a person entitled to the use and possession of a vehicle subject to a security interest in or lien by another person but excludes a lessee under a lease not intended as a security except as otherwise specifically provided in this title. 
Private road or driveway means every way or place in private ownership and used for vehicular traffic by the owner and those having express or implied permission from the owner, but not by other persons. 
Sidewalk means that portion of a street between the curb lines, or the lateral lines of a railway, and the adjacent property lines, intended for use by pedestrians. 
Street means the entire width between boundary lines of every way publicly maintained when any part thereof is open to the use of the public for purposes of vehicular travel. 
(Ord. of 9-3-2013) 
Sec. 70-83. - License required. 
Those persons who are 15 years of age, but not yet 16 years of age may drive a LSMV on the streets and those areas accessible by the public for vehicular traffic of the city provided he or she has in his or her possession a valid instructional permit issued by the state pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 40-5-4, as may be amended, and has not had his or her instructional permit suspended or revoked, and if he or she is accompanied in the front seat by a person at least 18 years of age who holds a valid motor vehicle driver's license. 
(Ord. of 9-3-2013) 
Sec. 70-84. - Operation regulations. 
(a)  All operators of LSMVs shall abide by all traffic regulations applicable to vehicular traffic when using the streets and those areas accessible by the public for vehicular traffic in the city. 
(b)  LSMVs shall not be operated on sidewalks at any time. 
(c)  LSMVs may be operated over those streets and those areas accessible by the public for vehicular traffic only during daylight hours unless such motorized carts are equipped with functional headlights, tail lights, and brake lights. 
(d)  LSMVs shall not be operated two or more abreast in a single traffic lane. 
(e)  LSMVs shall be operated only on any highway or streets where the posted speed limit does not exceed 35 miles per hour. The operator of an LSMV shall not operate such vehicle on any street or highway where the posted speed limit exceeds 35 miles per hour, as required by O.C.G.A. § 40-6-362 except state highways (1, 280, 152 and 292). LSMV may cross state highways perpendicular. 
(f)  The operator driving LSMVs shall not engage in hazardous activities on the highway or streets and those areas accessible by the public for vehicular traffic. Such hazardous activities, and the special rules pertaining to them, include but are not limited to the following: 
(1)  Racing of LSMV in any form, except for special events approved by the city; and 
(2)  Blocking of highway or streets and public access, for vehicular traffic, except for special events approved by the city. 
(g)  All laws and ordinances relative to alcohol and its use, including open container laws, which apply to traffic on the streets of the city, also apply to operators of LSMVs. 
(h)  All operators and passengers must remain seated at all times during the operation of the LSMV. No person may sit on the operator's lap during the operation of the LSMV. 
(i)  Before any LSMV may be operated upon city streets or public areas of the city, it shall have installed thereon: 
(1)  An emblem as required by O.C.G.A. § 40-8-4. The emblem shall be in a bright and conspicuous retro-reflective red-orange paint. Such emblem shall be mounted on the rear of such vehicles, in the approximate horizontal geometric center of the vehicle, at the height of three feet to five feet above the roadway, and shall be maintained at all times in a clean and reflective condition. 
(2)  An amber strobe light as required by O.C.G.A. § 40-8-35. The light must be functional at all times the vehicle is in operation, and shall be visible within 500 feet from the front and rear of the vehicle. 
(Ord. of 9-3-2013) 
Sec. 70-85. - Exemption. 
The provision of section 70-84 entitled "operating regulations" shall not apply to private streets or cart paths in subdivisions designed as golf course communities if such exemption is requested by the developer of such community or a homeowners association in writing and approved by the city. 
(Ord. of 9-3-2013) 
Sec. 70-86. - All-terrain vehicle. 
All-terrain vehicles shall not be operated on any street or highway, sidewalk within the city. 
(Ord. of 9-3-2013) 
Sec. 70-87. - Penalties. 
Any violation by an operator of a LSMV shall be charged against the operator according to the provisions of O.C.G.A. Title 40 and this article. 
(Ord. of 9-3-2013)

Chapter 74 - UTILITIES[1] 
Footnotes:
